Mahr When One Slave is Free: Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr when one of two slaves is free.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and Abu Yusuf's positions on mahr when a free person is mistakenly included as part of the dower, and apply the principle that a named mahr (musamma) prevents mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A named mahr stands even if part is invalid; the free person is excluded from the contract.

When a husband specifies two slaves as mahr but one is actually free, a dispute arises: does the wife receive only the valid slave, or also compensation for the free one? This lesson unpacks the reasoning of the two great Hanafi imams, focusing on the role of the named mahr and its exclusivity over mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Understand the scenario: a man gives two slaves as mahr, but one is free. State what each imam rules for the wife's entitlement.
Abu Hanifa gives only the slave (or its value up to 10 dirhams); Abu Yusuf gives the slave plus the value of the free person.
2
Extract Abu Hanifa's dalil
Identify why Abu Hanifa excludes the free person and upholds the named mahr. He argues that pointing to the free person (like 'the sea') removes him from the contract, and the named mahr, however small, prevents mahr al-mithl.
Key principle: musamma prevents mahr al-mithl.
3
Extract Abu Yusuf's dalil
Identify why Abu Yusuf adds compensation. He argues that the husband raised her expectations for both slaves and failed to deliver one, so its value is due.
Abu Yusuf focuses on the husband's inducement and inability to deliver.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the wife gets only the slave (or value up to 10); under Abu Yusuf, she gets the slave plus the value of the free person.
The difference is whether compensation for the invalid part is owed.
5
Apply the key principle
Explain how the principle 'a named mahr prevents mahr al-mithl' governs both positions: Abu Hanifa applies it strictly, while Abu Yusuf still respects the named mahr but adds compensation for the invalid part.
Both imams agree that musamma and mahr al-mithl do not combine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ں لئے کہ وہ مال نہیں ہے، تو اس کا ذکر کرنا لغو ہو گا، گویا نکاح ہوا مگر دوسرے غلام کے بدلے، لہذا یہی لازم ہوگا، مہر مثل لازم نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ مسمی کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوتا۔ (قَوْلُهُ وَإِذَا أَمْهَرَ عَبْدَيْنِ وَأَحَدُهُمَا حُرِّ فَمَهُرُهَا الْعَبْدُ يَعْنِي عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِذَا سَاوَى عَشَرَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَإِلَّا كَمُلَ لَهَا الْعَشَرَةُ، لِأَنَّهُ مُسَمًّى وَوُجُوبُ الْمُسَمَّى وَإِنْ قَلَّ يَمْنَعُ وُجُوبَ مَهْرِ الْمِثْلِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَهَا الْعَبْدُ وَقِيمَةُ الْحُرِّ لَوْ كَانَ عَبْدًا؛ لِأَنَّهُ أَطْمَعَهَا سَلَامَةَ الْعَبْدَيْنِ وَعَجَزَ عَنْ تَسْلِيمٍ أَحَدِهِمَا فَتَحِبُ قِيمَتُهُ. وَلِأَنَّ الْمُسَمَّى وَمَهْرَ الْمِثْلِ لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ بَيَانُ هَذِهِ أَنَّ أَبَا حَنِيفَةَ يَعْتَبِرُ الْإِشَارَةَ، وَالْإِشَارَةُ إِلَى الْبَحْرِ تُخْرِجُهُ عَنِ الْعَقْدِ، فَكَانَتْ تَسْمِيَةُ الْعَبْدِ الْبَاقِي لَغْوًا، فَكَأَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا عَلَى عَبْدٍ، وَلَيْسَ لَهَا إِلَّا ذَلِكَ، وَلَا يَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ لِأَنَّهُمَا لَا يَجْتَمِعَانِ.
...because he is not property, so mentioning him is futile, as if the marriage occurred in exchange for the other slave, so this is binding, and mahr al-mithl is not obligatory because it does not combine with the named mahr. (His statement: And if he gave two slaves as mahr and one of them is free, then her mahr is the slave, according to Abu Hanifa if it equals ten dirhams, otherwise she completes ten dirhams, because it is a named mahr and the obligation of the named mahr, even if small, prevents the obligation of mahr al-mithl. Abu Yusuf said: She gets the slave and the value of the free one as if he were a slave, because he gave her hope for both slaves and failed to deliver one, so its value is due. And because the named mahr and mahr al-mithl do not combine. The explanation is that Abu Hanifa considers the reference (to the sea) removes him from the contract, so the naming of the remaining slave is void, as if he married her for a slave, and she only has that, and mahr al-mithl is not obligatory because they do not combine.)
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding mahr when a man gives two slaves as dower but one is actually free. The author first summarizes the ruling: since the free person is not property, mentioning him is futile, so the valid mahr is the slave. Mahr al-mithl (proper dower) does not become due because a named mahr (musamma) and mahr al-mithl cannot coexist. Then the text quotes a longer ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the wife receives the slave if its value is at least ten dirhams; if less, she completes to ten dirhams. The reason is that the named mahr, however small, prevents mahr al-mithl. Imam Abu Yusuf differs: she receives the slave and also the value of the free person as if he were a slave, because the husband raised her expectations for both but failed to deliver one. Abu Hanifa's view is that the very act of pointing to the free person (referred to as 'the sea' in the source) removes him from the contract, so only the slave remains as named mahr. The key principle is that a named mahr, even if minimal, precludes the imposition of mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms
مهر مسمى (mahr musamma): The dower explicitly named in the marriage contract.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by the woman's peers when no dower is named.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the case of two slaves given as mahr, one free?
A) Under Abu Hanifa, the wife gets the slave; under Abu Yusuf, she gets the free person instead.
B) Under Abu Hanifa, the wife gets the slave (or value up to 10); under Abu Yusuf, she gets the slave plus the value of the free person.
C) Under Abu Hanifa, the wife gets mahr al-mithl; under Abu Yusuf, she gets the slave.
D) Under Abu Hanifa, the wife gets nothing; under Abu Yusuf, she gets the slave.

Key Takeaway
A named mahr (musamma) prevents mahr al-mithl, even if part of the named mahr is invalid, as long as at least one valid item remains.

Establishing Lineage in a Fasid Marriage
Legal maxim on establishing lineage cautiously for the child's sake.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling that lineage is established in a fasid marriage, EXPLAIN the maxim of caution (ihtiyat) and its basis in istihsan, and DISTINGUISH the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the timing of the duration.

Core Idea
Lineage is established in fasid marriage due to shubhah, applying istihsan to protect the child.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental Hanafi principle: lineage (nasab) is a matter of caution, established even in a defective marriage to preserve the child's welfare. The author of al-Hidayah invokes the maxim 'Lineage is established with caution to give life to the child' to justify a ruling that may seem counterintuitive: a child born from an irregular (fasid) marriage is still attributed to the father. This is a classic application of istihsan over strict qiyas. We will also explore a well-known intra-Hanafi difference on when the duration for lineage begins, and which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Governing Maxim
Read the maxim and its explanation. Understand that lineage is established with caution (ihtiyat) for the sake of giving life to the child. This is the core principle behind the ruling.
The maxim is not limited to fasid marriage—it reflects a general Hanafi attitude toward lineage.
2
Apply the Maxim to Fasid Marriage
Notice that in a fasid marriage, the contract contains offer and acceptance, creating a doubt (shubhah) of validity. The child's lineage is established because of this doubt, even though the marriage itself is defective.
This is a departure from strict qiyas, which would require a valid marriage or valid intercourse.
3
Recognize the Dalil (Istihsan)
The evidence for this ruling is istihsan—juristic preference based on the child's welfare. The text explicitly says 'lineage is established with caution to give life to the child.'
Istihsan overrides the requirement of a fully valid contract because of the higher objective of preserving the child.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Timing
There is a difference among the three imams: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf count the period for lineage from the contract (by analogy to valid marriage). Imam Muhammad counts it from actual intercourse. Understand the reasoning of each side.
The analogy (qiyas) to valid marriage is the basis for the earlier view; Imam Muhammad's view is based on the nature of fasid marriage not being a motivator for intercourse.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Later scholars (mashayikh) preferred Imam Muhammad's view because the analogy to valid marriage is weak. The relied-upon fatwa is that the duration is counted from intercourse.
This tarjih is based on the weakness of the qiyas, not on a direct text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٤) إِنَّ النَّسَبَ يُحْتَاطُ فِي إِثْبَاتِهِ إِحْيَاء لِلْوَلَدِ. ترجمہ: بچے کی افزائش زندگی کے لئے ثبوت نسب میں احتیاط برتی جاتی ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ والد کے نسب ثابت کرنے میں احتیاط برتی جاتی ہے، بچے کو زندگی دینے اور اس کے مستقبل کو سنورانے اور تابناک بنانے کے لئے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ نکاح فاسد میں بچے کا نسب ثابت ہوگا، یعنی اگر کسی شخص نے نکاح فاسد کیا اور اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا تو اس بچے کا نسب اس واطی سے ثابت ہوگا اور نسب کے ثبوت کی مدت کا اعتبار دخول کے وقت سے ہوگا ، اسی وقت سے مدت نسب کا اعتبار ہوگا ، اسی شوہر سے اس عورت کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہوگا کیونکہ یہ نکاح اگر چہ فاسد ہے مگر اس میں ایجاب وقبول موجود ہے، اس لئے اس میں نکاح صحیح کا بھی شبہ ہے، لہذا اس شبہ کو بنیاد بنا کر اس پر نسب کا ترتب ہو گا۔ اگر نسب کو ثابت نہ مانا جائے تو بچے کے لئے کوئی مربی نہیں ہوگا، بچہ ضائع ہو جائے گا اور اس کا مستقبل تاریک ہو جائے گا۔ (وَيَثْبُتُ النَّسَبُ) أَى نَسَبُ الْوَلَدِ الْمَوْلُودِ فِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ يُحْتَاطُ فِي إِثْبَاتِهِ إحْيَاء لِلْوَلَدِ فَيَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَى الثَّابِتِ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ مُدَّةُ النَّسَبِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الدُّخُولِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى؛ لِأَنَّ النِّكَاحَ الْفَاسِدَ لَيْسَ بِدَاعِ إِلَيْهِ وَالْإِقَامَةُ بِاعْتِبَارِهِ كَذَا فِي الْهِدَايَةِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ ابْتِدَاءُ الْمُدَّةِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الْعَقْدِ قِيَاسًا عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ وَالْمَشَايِخُ أَفْتَوُا بِقَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ لِبُعْدِ قَوْلِهِمَا لِعَدَمٍ صِحَّةِ الْقِيَاسِ الْمَذْكُورِ.
(24) Indeed, lineage is observed with caution in establishing it, giving life to the child. Translation: Caution is exercised in establishing lineage for the child's upbringing. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that caution is used in establishing the father's lineage, to give life to the child and improve his future. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to state that in a fasid marriage, the child's lineage is established. That is, if a person contracts a fasid marriage and a child is born, the child's lineage is established from the one who had intercourse. The duration for lineage is counted from the time of intercourse. This is because although the marriage is fasid, it contains offer and acceptance, so there is a doubt (shubhah) of a valid marriage. Based on this doubt, lineage is attached. If lineage were not established, the child would have no guardian, would be lost, and his future dark. (And lineage is established) meaning the lineage of a child born in a fasid marriage, because lineage is observed with caution in its establishment to give life to the child, so it is attached to what is established in some way. The duration of lineage is counted from the time of intercourse according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and the fatwa is upon this, because the fasid marriage does not necessitate it, and residence is considered accordingly in al-Hidayah. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the beginning of the duration is from the time of the contract, by analogy to a valid marriage. The mashayikh gave fatwa with Muhammad's view because their view is far-fetched and the analogy is invalid.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim and its application from the Hanafi school. The maxim (24) states: 'Lineage is established with caution for the sake of giving life to the child.' The author explains that this principle is applied in the case of a fasid (irregular) marriage. Although the marriage is invalid due to some defect, the child's lineage is still established from the father because the contract contains offer and acceptance, creating a doubt (shubhah) of a valid marriage. This istihsan (juristic preference) overrides the strict requirement of a valid marriage, preserving the child's welfare. The text then discusses the timing: according to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the period for considering lineage (minimum six months) begins from actual intercourse (dukhul), and this is the relied-upon fatwa. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf say it begins from the time of the contract, analogizing to a valid marriage. However, later scholars (mashayikh) preferred Imam Muhammad's view because the analogy to a valid marriage is weak—since a fasid marriage does not call for lineage like a valid one does. The ruling is an example of istihsan based on the need to protect the child.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or parentage of a child, established through valid or doubtful marriage.
نکاح فاسد (nikah fasid): A marriage that is invalid due to a deficiency in conditions or pillars but has offer and acceptance.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Legal caution, preferring the safer ruling to avoid harm, here to preserve lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view, from when is the period for establishing lineage counted in a fasid marriage?
A) From the time of the marriage contract
B) From the time of actual intercourse
C) From the time of the child's birth
D) From the time of the woman's statement

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, lineage is established in a fasid marriage due to shubhah and istihsan, with the duration counted from intercourse (mufta bihi).

The Maxim: A Person Belongs to His Father's People
Legal maxim with application to mahr al-mithl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim of paternal lineage and apply it to determine the basis for mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A person's lineage follows the father; thus mahr al-mithl is based on the father's tribe, not the mother's.

This lesson unpacks a concise legal maxim from Al-Hidayah that anchors lineage to the father. Though seemingly straightforward, its application to determining the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) carries significant practical implications. We will see how the Hanafi school uses this principle to establish a consistent valuation for a woman's dower when no amount is specified, and why the paternal side is given exclusive weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
Read the Arabic maxim and its translation. Understand that it asserts a person belongs to the 'jins' (kin/type) of his father's people. The key is that lineage and social category are determined by the father.
The term 'jins' here means lineage or type, not biological sex.
2
Connect to Mahr al-Mithl
The author applies the maxim to mahr al-mithl. Identify that mahr al-mithl is the proper dower for a woman when no dower was specified in the marriage contract. According to the maxim, the woman's 'peers' for determining her dower are her paternal female relatives: sisters, paternal aunts, and paternal cousins.
Mahr al-Mithl is wajib in such cases.
3
Note the Exception
Examine the exception: if the mother is also from the father's tribe (e.g., a paternal cousin), then the mother's mahr may be considered. This is because she belongs to the same paternal lineage, so she is a peer.
This exception reinforces the rule—it does not introduce maternal lineage generally.
4
Grasp the Legal Reasoning
The underlying reasoning is qiyas: the value (price) of something is determined by its peers (misl). Since a woman's peers are her paternal relatives (following lineage), mahr al-mithl is based on them. This ensures consistency and objectivity.
This is a form of istidlal (reasoning) by analogy to the valuation of commodities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۵) إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمٍ أَبِيهِ. ترجمہ: انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کی جنس سے ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کی جنس میں سے ہوتا ہے، یعنی جنسیت میں باپ کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور نسبت بھی باپ کی طرف ہوتی ہے، بایں وجہ مہر مثل میں بھی باپ کے قبیلے کی عورتوں کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ عورت کے مہر مثل کا اعتبار اس کی بہنوں اور پھوپھیوں اور چچا زاد بہنوں کے ساتھ ہوگا، یعنی باپ کی طرف جو قبیلہ ہے اس کی عورتوں کے ساتھ مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہو گا اور ماں کی طرف سے جو قبیلہ ہے اس کی عورتوں کا اعتبار نہیں ہو گا۔ البتہ اگر ماں بھی باپ کے قبیلے میں سے ہو جیسے ماں باپ کی چچا زاد ہو تو اس صورت میں ماں کے مہر مثل کا بھی اعتبار ہو گا ورنہ نہیں ، کیونکہ ہر انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کا ہم جنس ہوتا ہے اور ہر شے کی قیمت اس کی ہم جنس چیز میں غور کرنے سے معلوم ہوتی ہے، اس لئے والد کی قرابت دار
(25) Indeed, a person is of the kin of his father's people. Translation: A person belongs to the people of his father. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that a person is from the kin of his father's people, meaning lineage is considered through the father, and lineage is attributed to the father. Therefore, in mahr al-mithl, the women of the father's tribe are considered. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to state that a woman's mahr al-mithl is based on her sisters, paternal aunts, and female paternal cousins. That is, the women of the father's tribe are considered for mahr al-mithl, not the women of the mother's tribe. However, if the mother is also from the father's tribe (e.g., she is the father's cousin), then the mother's mahr al-mithl is also considered, otherwise not. Because every person is of the same kind as his father's people, and the price of something is determined by considering its peers, so the father's relatives...
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the maxim (25): 'A person belongs to the people of his father.' The author applies it to the determination of mahr al-mithl (proper dower). In the Hanafi school, when a woman's dower is not specified in the marriage contract, mahr al-mithl is calculated based on the women of her paternal tribe—her sisters, paternal aunts, and paternal female cousins. The maternal side is not considered because lineage follows the father. An exception occurs if the mother herself is from the father's tribe (e.g., she is a paternal cousin), then her mahr may also be considered because she belongs to the same paternal line. The underlying reasoning is that a person's value is determined by their peers, and a woman's peers are her paternal relatives, not maternal. This principle ensures consistency in valuation.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Kin or type; here referring to paternal lineage determining a person's category.
قبیلہ (qabilah): Tribe or clan, specifically the father's tribe for lineage.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by the dower of women of equal status to the bride.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, which relatives are considered for determining a woman's mahr al-mithl?
A) Her mother's sisters and maternal aunts
B) Her father's sisters and paternal aunts
C) Both paternal and maternal equally
D) Only her sisters

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim that a person belongs to his father's people exclusively determines mahr al-mithl based on paternal female relatives.

intermediate

Mahr al-Mithl: Determining the Proper Dower Based on Paternal Lineage
Principle and application to mahr al-mithl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle 'al-insan min jins qawm abihi' and apply it to identify which female relatives are considered in determining mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A woman's proper dower is benchmarked against her paternal female relatives, not maternal, because a person's lineage follows the father.

What determines the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) of a bride? The Hanafi school answers with a powerful principle: a person is of the kind of his father's people. This lesson unpacks that principle and shows how it governs the selection of comparable women for dower assessment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What is mahr al-mithl and why is it needed? It is the appropriate dower when no specific dower is fixed or when the marriage is fasid and consummated.
Mahr al-mithl ensures fairness by comparing the woman to her peers.
2
State the principle
The passage states: 'Indeed, the human is of the kind of his father's people.' This is the foundational maxim (al-usul).
Recognize that this is a qiyas-based principle, not directly from nass.
3
Apply the principle to mahr
The value of a thing is known by its kind. Since the woman's lineage follows her father, her worth (mahr) is compared to her paternal female relatives: sisters, paternal aunts, female paternal cousins.
Maternal relatives are excluded unless they are also from the father's tribe.
4
Identify the attributes for comparison
The passage specifies that the comparable woman must be similar in beauty, age, wealth, and virginity. These attributes affect the mahr.
Other factors like education or profession are not mentioned; these classical criteria are still relevant.
5
Consider the exception
If the mother is from the father's tribe (e.g., paternal cousin), then her mahr may also be considered, but not because she is mother—rather because she is a paternal relative.
This reinforces that paternal lineage is the decisive factor.

اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی
(۲۵) إِنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمٍ أَبِيهِ.
ترجمہ: انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کی جنس سے ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کی جنس میں سے ہوتا ہے، یعنی جنسیت میں باپ کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور نسبت بھی باپ کی طرف ہوتی ہے، بایں وجہ مہر مثل میں بھی باپ کے قبیلے کی عورتوں کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ عورت کے مہر مثل کا اعتبار اس کی بہنوں اور پھوپھیوں اور چچا زاد بہنوں کے ساتھ ہوگا، یعنی باپ کی طرف جو قبیلہ ہے اس کی عورتوں کے ساتھ مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہو گا اور ماں کی طرف سے جو قبیلہ ہے اس کی عورتوں کا اعتبار نہیں ہو گا۔ البتہ اگر ماں بھی باپ کے قبیلے میں سے ہو جیسے ماں باپ کی چچا زاد ہو تو اس صورت میں ماں کے مہر مثل کا بھی اعتبار ہو گا ورنہ نہیں ، کیونکہ ہر انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کا ہم جنس ہوتا ہے اور ہر شے کی قیمت اس کی ہم جنس چیز میں غور کرنے سے معلوم ہوتی ہے، اس لئے والد کی قرابت دار (وَيَثْبُتُ النَّسَبُ) أَى نَسَبُ الْوَلَدِ الْمَوْلُودِ فِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ يُحْتَاطُ فِي إِثْبَاتِهِ إحْيَاء لِلْوَلَدِ فَيَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَى الثَّابِتِ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ مُدَّةُ النَّسَبِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الدُّخُولِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى.
تبيين الحقائق: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۱۵۳، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية (قَوْلُهُ وَيَثْبُتُ النَّسَبُ أَى نَسَبُ الْمَوْلُودِ فِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ، لَّانَّ النَّسَبَ مِمَّا يُحْتَاطُ فِي إِثْبَاتِهِ إِحْيَاء لِلْوَلَدِ فَيَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَى الثَّابِتِ مِنْ وَجْهِ أَطْلَقَهُ فَأَفَادَ أَنَّهُ يَثْبُتُ بِغَيْرِ دَعْوَةٍ كَمَا فِي الْقُنْيَةِ وَتُعْتَبَرُ مُدَّةُ النَّسَبِ وَهِيَ سِتَّةُ أَشْهُرٍ مِنْ وَقْتِ الدُّخُولِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى؛ لِأَنَّ النِّكَاحَ الْفَاسِدَ لَيْسَ بِدَاعِ إِلَيْهِ وَالْإِقَامَةُ بِاعْتِبَارِهِ كَذَا فِي الْهِدَايَةِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ ابْتِدَاءُ الْمُدَّةِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الْعَقْدِ قِيَاسًا عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ وَالْمَشَايِخُ أَفْتَوُا بِقَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ لِبُعْدِ قَوْلِهِمَا لِعَدَمٍ صِحَّةِ الْقِيَاسِ الْمَذْكُورِ
البحر الرائق: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر ، ج ۳ ص ۱۸۴ ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
الهداية: كتاب النكاح ، باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۴، ط: رحمانیه
وَلَكِنَّا نَقُولُ: قِيمَةُ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالرُّجُوعِ إِلَى قِيمَةِ جِنْسِهِ، وَالْإِنْسَانُ مِنْ جِئْسِ قَوْمِ أَبِيهِ لَا مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمٍ أُمِّهِ، أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْأُمَّ قَدْ تَكُونُ أَمَةً، وَالْبِئْتُ تَكُونُ قُرَشِيَّةٌ تَبَعًا لَّا بِيهَا فَلِهَذَا اُعْتُبِرَ عَشِيرَتُهَا مِنْ قِبَلِ أَبِيهَا ، وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ مَهْرُهَا بِمَهْرٍ أُمِّهَا إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ أُمُّهَا مِنْ قَوْمٍ أَبِيهَا بِأَنْ كَانَتْ بِنْتَ عَمِّهِ، فَحِينَئِذٍ يُعْتَبَرُ مَهْرُهَا لَا لِأَنَّهَا أُمَّهَا بَلْ، لِأَنَّهَا بِئْتُ عَمِّ أَبِيهَا، وَإِنَّمَا يُعْتَبَرُ مِنْ عَشِيرَتِهَا امْرَأَةٌ هِيَ مِثْلُهَا فِي الْحُسْنِ، وَالْجَمَالِ وَالسِّنِّ وَالْمَالِ وَالْبَكَارَةِ، لَّانَّ الْمُهُورَ تَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِ هَذِهِ الْأَوْصَافِ.
المبسوط للسرخسي کتاب النکاح باب المهر، ج ۵ ص ۶۴، ط: دار المعرفة وَإِنَّمَا يُضَافُ إِلَى أَقَارِبِ الأب لأنَّ النَّسَبَ إِلَيْهِ، وَلَأنَّ قِيمَةَ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالرُّجُوعِ إِلَى قِيمَةِ جِنْسِهِ وَالْإِنْسَانُ مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمِ أَبِيهِ لَا مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمٍ أُمِّهِ؛ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْأُمَّ قَدْ تَكُونُ أَمَةً وَالابْنَةَ تَكُونُ قُرَشِيَّةٌ تَبَعًا لِأَبِيهَا وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ بِأُمِّهَا وَخَالَتِهَا إِذَا لَمْ تَكُونَا مِنْ قَبِيلَتِهَا) بِأَنْ يَكُونَ أَبُوهَا تَزَوَّجَ بِنْتَ عَمِّهِ فَإِنَّ أُمَّهَا وَخَالَتَهَا تَكُونُ مِنْ قَبِيلَتِهَا. وَقَوْلُهُ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا) إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ وَقِيمَةُ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالنَّظَرِ فِي قِيمَةِ جِنسِهِ.
العناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۳۶۸، ط: دار الفكر
الهداية كتاب النكاح باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۶، ط: رحمانیه
Principles of Hidayah Volume Two (25) Indeed, the human is of the kind of his father's people. Translation: A human is of the kind of his father's people. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that a human is of the kind of his father's people, meaning that in lineage the father is considered and relation is also to the father. For this reason, in mahr al-mithl, the women of the father's tribe are considered. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning the aforementioned principle, is stating that consideration for the mahr al-mithl of a woman will be with her sisters, paternal aunts, and female paternal cousins, i.e., consideration will be with the women of her father's tribe, and consideration will not be with the women of her mother's tribe. However, if the mother is also from the father's tribe, such as if the mother is the father's cousin, then in that case the mother's mahr al-mithl will also be considered; otherwise not, because every human is of the same kind as his father's people, and the value of everything is known by considering its like-kind. Therefore, the paternal relatives (and lineage is established) i.e., the lineage of a child born in a fasid (irregular) marriage, because lineage is treated with caution in its establishment to give life to the child, so it is established from some aspect. And the period for lineage is considered from the time of consummation according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and on that is the fatwa. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2 p. 153, al-Matba'ah al-Kubra al-Amiriyya (His statement: 'And lineage is established' i.e., lineage of a child born in a fasid marriage, because lineage is among matters that are treated with caution in their establishment to give life to the child, so it is established from some aspect. He made it absolute, thus indicating that it is established without a claim (da'wa), as in al-Qunyah. And the period for lineage, which is six months, is considered from the time of consummation according to Muhammad, and on that is the fatwa; because the fasid marriage does not call for it, and the stay (of the husband) is considered due to it. Thus in al-Hidayah. And according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the beginning of the period is from the time of the contract, by analogy with a valid marriage. And the mashayikh (later scholars) gave fatwa according to Muhammad's view due to the weakness of their view because of the soundness of the analogy mentioned. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 3 p. 184, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2 p. 354, Rahmaniyya. But we say: The value of a thing is known only by referring to the value of its kind, and the human is of the kind of his father's people, not of the kind of his mother's people. Do you not see that the mother may be a slave-girl, and the daughter is Qurayshi by following her father? So for this, her paternal relatives are considered, and her mahr is not considered by her mother's mahr unless her mother is from her father's people, such as if she was his paternal cousin. Then in that case her mahr is considered; not because she is her mother, but because she is the paternal cousin of her father. And consideration is only for a woman from her paternal relatives who is similar to her in good looks, beauty, age, wealth, and virginity, because mahr differs with the difference of these attributes. Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 5 p. 64, Dar al-Ma'rifa. And it is attributed to paternal relatives because lineage is to him, and because the value of a thing is known only by referring to the value of its kind, and the human is of the kind of his father's people, not of the kind of his mother's people. Do you not see that the mother may be a slave-girl and the daughter is Qurayshi following her father, and she is not compared to her mother or maternal aunt if they are not from her tribe? If her father married his paternal cousin, then her mother and maternal aunt are from her tribe. And his statement 'because we have explained' refers to his statement 'and the value of a thing is known only by looking at the value of its kind.' Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 3 p. 368, Dar al-Fikr. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2 p. 356, Rahmaniyya.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the 25th usul (principle) from Usool al-Hidayah: 'Indeed, the human is of the kind of his father's people.' The author uses this principle to resolve two fiqh issues: (1) determining mahr al-mithl (the proper dower for a woman) and (2) establishing lineage (nasab) in a fasid (irregular) marriage. For mahr al-mithl, the woman's paternal female relatives (sisters, paternal aunts, female paternal cousins) are the benchmark because value is determined by like-kind, and a person's kind follows the father's lineage. The mother's female relatives are irrelevant unless they are also from the father's tribe (e.g., if the mother is the father's cousin). For lineage in a fasid marriage, the child's lineage is established from the time of consummation according to Imam Muhammad (and this is the relied-upon fatwa) because the marriage is not a valid cause for the child. The six-month minimum gestation period is counted from the date of consummation. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf analogize to a valid marriage and count from the contract date, but later scholars (mashayikh) preferred Muhammad's view because the analogy is weak. The passage quotes multiple Hanafi sources (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Mabsut, al-'Inayah) all confirming this principle.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower for a woman of similar status, determined by considering the dowers of her paternal female relatives (sisters, paternal aunts, female paternal cousins) who are similar in beauty, age, wealth, and virginity.
جنس (jins): Kind, type, or genus. In this context, the lineage or kind that determines worth and legal standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'al-insan min jins qawm abihi,' which relatives are used to determine the mahr al-mithl of a woman?
A) Her maternal aunts and cousins.
B) Her sisters, paternal aunts, and female paternal cousins.
C) All her female relatives equally.
D) Only her mother's mahr.

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is determined by the dowers of the woman's paternal female relatives who are similar in key attributes, because a person's lineage and worth follow the father.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Establishing Lineage (Nasab) in a Fasid Marriage: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Timing
Dispute on start of gestation period for nasab in fasid nikah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn on the start of the six-month gestation period in a fasid marriage, and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
In a fasid marriage, lineage is established from the time of consummation, not the contract, because precaution (ihtiyat) overrides weak analogy.

A fasid marriage does not automatically make a child legitimate, but Hanafi fiqh protects the child by cautiously establishing lineage. A key dispute arises: does the six-month minimum gestation start from the marriage contract or from actual consummation? This lesson explores the Hanafi internal difference and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
A child is born in a fasid marriage. The court must determine if the child's lineage is established to the father. The key condition is that at least six months have passed between the relevant starting point and the birth.
Fasid marriage includes defects like absence of wali or marrying a fifth wife.
2
State the agreed principle
All Hanafi imams agree that lineage is established cautiously, to protect the child's life. The child's nasab is established from 'some aspect' (min wajh).
The cautious approach reflects the maxim that lineage is a matter where caution is applied.
3
Identify the dispute
What is the starting point for the six-month period? Imam Muhammad says from the time of consummation (dukhul). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say from the time of the marriage contract (aqd).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the evidence for each side
Muhammad's dalil: The fasid marriage is not a cause (da'i) for the child; the marriage does not necessarily lead to consummation. The husband's stay is only considered from actual consummation. The Sahibayn's dalil: By analogy (qiyas) to a valid marriage, where the period is counted from the contract.
The analogy is based on the similarity of outward form of marriage.
5
Determine the tarjih
Later scholars (mashayikh) preferred Muhammad's view because the analogy to a valid marriage is weak; a valid marriage is a cause, a fasid is not. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view.
The thamarah: If a woman gives birth more than 6 months after consummation but less than 6 months after contract, lineage is established per Muhammad, not per Sahibayn.

تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کی جنس میں سے ہوتا ہے، یعنی جنسیت میں باپ کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور نسبت بھی باپ کی طرف ہوتی ہے، بایں وجہ مہر مثل میں بھی باپ کے قبیلے کی عورتوں کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ عورت کے مہر مثل کا اعتبار اس کی بہنوں اور پھوپھیوں اور چچا زاد بہنوں کے ساتھ ہوگا، یعنی باپ کی طرف جو قبیلہ ہے اس کی عورتوں کے ساتھ مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہو گا اور ماں کی طرف سے جو قبیلہ ہے اس کی عورتوں کا اعتبار نہیں ہو گا۔ البتہ اگر ماں بھی باپ کے قبیلے میں سے ہو جیسے ماں باپ کی چچا زاد ہو تو اس صورت میں ماں کے مہر مثل کا بھی اعتبار ہو گا ورنہ نہیں ، کیونکہ ہر انسان اپنے باپ کی قوم کا ہم جنس ہوتا ہے اور ہر شے کی قیمت اس کی ہم جنس چیز میں غور کرنے سے معلوم ہوتی ہے، اس لئے والد کی قرابت دار (وَيَثْبُتُ النَّسَبُ) أَى نَسَبُ الْوَلَدِ الْمَوْلُودِ فِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ يُحْتَاطُ فِي إِثْبَاتِهِ إحْيَاء لِلْوَلَدِ فَيَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَى الثَّابِتِ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ مُدَّةُ النَّسَبِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الدُّخُولِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى.
تبيين الحقائق: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۱۵۳، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية (قَوْلُهُ وَيَثْبُتُ النَّسَبُ أَى نَسَبُ الْمَوْلُودِ فِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ، لَّانَّ النَّسَبَ مِمَّا يُحْتَاطُ فِي إِثْبَاتِهِ إِحْيَاء لِلْوَلَدِ فَيَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَى الثَّابِتِ مِنْ وَجْهِ أَطْلَقَهُ فَأَفَادَ أَنَّهُ يَثْبُتُ بِغَيْرِ دَعْوَةٍ كَمَا فِي الْقُنْيَةِ وَتُعْتَبَرُ مُدَّةُ النَّسَبِ وَهِيَ سِتَّةُ أَشْهُرٍ مِنْ وَقْتِ الدُّخُولِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَيْهِ الْفَتْوَى؛ لِأَنَّ النِّكَاحَ الْفَاسِدَ لَيْسَ بِدَاعِ إِلَيْهِ وَالْإِقَامَةُ بِاعْتِبَارِهِ كَذَا فِي الْهِدَايَةِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ ابْتِدَاءُ الْمُدَّةِ مِنْ وَقْتِ الْعَقْدِ قِيَاسًا عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ وَالْمَشَايِخُ أَفْتَوُا بِقَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ لِبُعْدِ قَوْلِهِمَا لِعَدَمٍ صِحَّةِ الْقِيَاسِ الْمَذْكُورِ
البحر الرائق: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر ، ج ۳ ص ۱۸۴ ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
الهداية: كتاب النكاح ، باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۴، ط: رحمانیه
وَلَكِنَّا نَقُولُ: قِيمَةُ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالرُّجُوعِ إِلَى قِيمَةِ جِنْسِهِ، وَالْإِنْسَانُ مِنْ جِئْسِ قَوْمِ أَبِيهِ لَا مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمٍ أُمِّهِ، أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْأُمَّ قَدْ تَكُونُ أَمَةً، وَالْبِئْتُ تَكُونُ قُرَشِيَّةٌ تَبَعًا لَّا بِيهَا فَلِهَذَا اُعْتُبِرَ عَشِيرَتُهَا مِنْ قِبَلِ أَبِيهَا ، وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ مَهْرُهَا بِمَهْرٍ أُمِّهَا إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ أُمُّهَا مِنْ قَوْمٍ أَبِيهَا بِأَنْ كَانَتْ بِنْتَ عَمِّهِ، فَحِينَئِذٍ يُعْتَبَرُ مَهْرُهَا لَا لِأَنَّهَا أُمَّهَا بَلْ، لِأَنَّهَا بِئْتُ عَمِّ أَبِيهَا، وَإِنَّمَا يُعْتَبَرُ مِنْ عَشِيرَتِهَا امْرَأَةٌ هِيَ مِثْلُهَا فِي الْحُسْنِ، وَالْجَمَالِ وَالسِّنِّ وَالْمَالِ وَالْبَكَارَةِ، لَّانَّ الْمُهُورَ تَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِ هَذِهِ الْأَوْصَافِ.
المبسوط للسرخسي کتاب النکاح باب المهر، ج ۵ ص ۶۴، ط: دار المعرفة وَإِنَّمَا يُضَافُ إِلَى أَقَارِبِ الأب لأنَّ النَّسَبَ إِلَيْهِ، وَلَأنَّ قِيمَةَ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالرُّجُوعِ إِلَى قِيمَةِ جِنْسِهِ وَالْإِنْسَانُ مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمِ أَبِيهِ لَا مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمٍ أُمِّهِ؛ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْأُمَّ قَدْ تَكُونُ أَمَةً وَالابْنَةَ تَكُونُ قُرَشِيَّةٌ تَبَعًا لِأَبِيهَا وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ بِأُمِّهَا وَخَالَتِهَا إِذَا لَمْ تَكُونَا مِنْ قَبِيلَتِهَا) بِأَنْ يَكُونَ أَبُوهَا تَزَوَّجَ بِنْتَ عَمِّهِ فَإِنَّ أُمَّهَا وَخَالَتَهَا تَكُونُ مِنْ قَبِيلَتِهَا. وَقَوْلُهُ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا) إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ وَقِيمَةُ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالنَّظَرِ فِي قِيمَةِ جِنسِهِ.
العناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۳۶۸، ط: دار الفكر
الهداية كتاب النكاح باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۶، ط: رحمانیه
Principles of Hidayah Volume Two (25) Indeed, the human is of the kind of his father's people. Translation: A human is of the kind of his father's people. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that a human is of the kind of his father's people, meaning that in lineage the father is considered and relation is also to the father. For this reason, in mahr al-mithl, the women of the father's tribe are considered. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning the aforementioned principle, is stating that consideration for the mahr al-mithl of a woman will be with her sisters, paternal aunts, and female paternal cousins, i.e., consideration will be with the women of her father's tribe, and consideration will not be with the women of her mother's tribe. However, if the mother is also from the father's tribe, such as if the mother is the father's cousin, then in that case the mother's mahr al-mithl will also be considered; otherwise not, because every human is of the same kind as his father's people, and the value of everything is known by considering its like-kind. Therefore, the paternal relatives (and lineage is established) i.e., the lineage of a child born in a fasid (irregular) marriage, because lineage is treated with caution in its establishment to give life to the child, so it is established from some aspect. And the period for lineage is considered from the time of consummation according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and on that is the fatwa. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2 p. 153, al-Matba'ah al-Kubra al-Amiriyya (His statement: 'And lineage is established' i.e., lineage of a child born in a fasid marriage, because lineage is among matters that are treated with caution in their establishment to give life to the child, so it is established from some aspect. He made it absolute, thus indicating that it is established without a claim (da'wa), as in al-Qunyah. And the period for lineage, which is six months, is considered from the time of consummation according to Muhammad, and on that is the fatwa; because the fasid marriage does not call for it, and the stay (of the husband) is considered due to it. Thus in al-Hidayah. And according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the beginning of the period is from the time of the contract, by analogy with a valid marriage. And the mashayikh (later scholars) gave fatwa according to Muhammad's view due to the weakness of their view because of the soundness of the analogy mentioned. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 3 p. 184, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2 p. 354, Rahmaniyya. But we say: The value of a thing is known only by referring to the value of its kind, and the human is of the kind of his father's people, not of the kind of his mother's people. Do you not see that the mother may be a slave-girl, and the daughter is Qurayshi by following her father? So for this, her paternal relatives are considered, and her mahr is not considered by her mother's mahr unless her mother is from her father's people, such as if she was his paternal cousin. Then in that case her mahr is considered; not because she is her mother, but because she is the paternal cousin of her father. And consideration is only for a woman from her paternal relatives who is similar to her in good looks, beauty, age, wealth, and virginity, because mahr differs with the difference of these attributes. Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 5 p. 64, Dar al-Ma'rifa. And it is attributed to paternal relatives because lineage is to him, and because the value of a thing is known only by referring to the value of its kind, and the human is of the kind of his father's people, not of the kind of his mother's people. Do you not see that the mother may be a slave-girl and the daughter is Qurayshi following her father, and she is not compared to her mother or maternal aunt if they are not from her tribe? If her father married his paternal cousin, then her mother and maternal aunt are from her tribe. And his statement 'because we have explained' refers to his statement 'and the value of a thing is known only by looking at the value of its kind.' Al-'Inayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 3 p. 368, Dar al-Fikr. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2 p. 356, Rahmaniyya.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the 25th usul (principle) from Usool al-Hidayah: 'Indeed, the human is of the kind of his father's people.' The author uses this principle to resolve two fiqh issues: (1) determining mahr al-mithl (the proper dower for a woman) and (2) establishing lineage (nasab) in a fasid (irregular) marriage. For mahr al-mithl, the woman's paternal female relatives (sisters, paternal aunts, female paternal cousins) are the benchmark because value is determined by like-kind, and a person's kind follows the father's lineage. The mother's female relatives are irrelevant unless they are also from the father's tribe (e.g., if the mother is the father's cousin). For lineage in a fasid marriage, the child's lineage is established from the time of consummation according to Imam Muhammad (and this is the relied-upon fatwa) because the marriage is not a valid cause for the child. The six-month minimum gestation period is counted from the date of consummation. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf analogize to a valid marriage and count from the contract date, but later scholars (mashayikh) preferred Muhammad's view because the analogy is weak. The passage quotes multiple Hanafi sources (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Mabsut, al-'Inayah) all confirming this principle.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or parentage, specifically the child's legal affiliation to the father. In a fasid marriage, lineage is established cautiously to protect the child, even if the marriage itself is irregular.
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An irregular marriage that meets the essential elements (offer and acceptance, witnesses) but has a defect (e.g., lack of wali, marrying a fifth wife while still married to four). It is not void but can be validated by removing the defect.
داعٍ (da'in): A cause or effective reason that leads to a legal effect. In this context, a valid marriage is a cause for the child, while a fasid marriage is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which scholar's view is the fatwa for establishing nasab in a fasid marriage based?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
In a fasid marriage, the six-month gestation period for establishing lineage starts from the time of actual consummation, not from the marriage contract, because precaution for the child overrides weak analogy.

The Rule of Preponderant Apparent Circumstance in Claims: Applied to Mahr Disputes
Presenting the principle that in disputes, the word is of the one whose claim is supported by apparent circumstance, applied to mahr disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi evidentiary principle 'al-qawl li-man yashhadu lahu al-zahir' to resolve mahr disputes between spouses.

Core Idea
In a mahr dispute, the wife’s word is accepted up to mahr al-mithl; beyond that, the husband’s word prevails.

When spouses disagree on the mahr amount and neither has proof, the judge cannot simply guess. The Hanafi school provides a clear principle: the party whose claim matches the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) gets precedence. This lesson unpacks that maxim and shows its precise application to mahr conflicts.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Identify the maxim: 'In claims, the word is of the one whom the apparent circumstance supports according to both parties.' Understand that 'apparent circumstance' means external evidence or common practice.
This principle is not arbitrary; it is based on the idea that the truth is more likely to align with observable norms.
2
Identify the specific dispute
Recognize the scenario: husband and wife differ on the mahr amount. She claims a higher amount; he claims a lower one.
The dispute assumes no written contract or witnesses.
3
Apply the zahir analysis
Determine the mahr al-mithl (the proper dower for a woman of her status). This is the apparent circumstance. Then compare each party's claim to the mahr al-mithl.
The wife's claim up to mahr al-mithl is consistent with the zahir; her claim beyond that is not. The husband's claim is consistent with the zahir only if it does not exceed mahr al-mithl.
4
Determine the operative ruling
Apply the maxim: the wife's word is accepted for the amount up to mahr al-mithl; the husband's word is accepted for any amount exceeding that. This resolves the dispute.
The result is that the wife receives at least mahr al-mithl, and any additional amount she fails to prove is not awarded.
5
Note the thamarah (practical difference)
Understand that without this principle, the judge would have no basis to decide. The principle balances the burden of proof based on external plausibility.
The ruling is procedural, not a substantive obligation; it guides the court's decision-making.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی
(٢٦) إِنَّ الْقَوْلَ فِى الدَّعَاوَى قَوْلُ مَنْ يَشْهَدُ لَهُ الظَّاهِرُ عِنْدَ الطَّرَفَيْنِ.
ترجمہ: طرفین کے نزدیک دعووں میں اُس شخص کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے جس کے حق میں ظاہر حال شاہد ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دعووں میں اس شخص کے قول کا اعتبار ہو گا جس کے لئے ظاہر حال شاہد ہو یعنی جس کا قول ظاہر کے موافق ہو۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر میاں بیوی کا مہر میں اختلاف ہو گیا یعنی عورت زیادہ مہر کا دعوی کرتی ہے اور شوہر اس زیادتی کا انکار کرتا ہے، تو اس صورت میں مہر مثل کے مکمل ہونے کی حد تک عورت کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور مہرمل سے زیادہ کی صورت میں شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
Principles of Hidayah Volume Two (26) Indeed, in claims, the word is of the one whom the apparent circumstance supports according to both parties. Translation: According to both parties, in claims, the statement of that person is authoritative who has the apparent evidence in his favor. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that in claims, the statement of that person will be authoritative for whom the apparent circumstance is a witness, i.e., whose statement is in accordance with the apparent. The author of Hidayah, mentioning the aforementioned principle, is explaining that if a dispute occurs between husband and wife regarding the mahr, i.e., the woman claims a higher mahr and the husband denies this increase, then in that case, up to the completion of the mahr al-mithl, the woman's statement is authoritative, and beyond the mahr al-mithl, the husband's statement is authoritative.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents the 26th usul (principle) from Usool al-Hidayah: 'Indeed, in claims, the word is of the one whom the apparent circumstance supports according to both parties.' This is a general legal maxim in evidence law: when there is a dispute and no clear proof, the party whose claim is consistent with the external circumstances (al-zahir) is given precedence. The author applies this to a specific case: a dispute between husband and wife over the amount of mahr. The wife claims a high mahr; the husband claims a lower amount. The ruling: up to the amount of mahr al-mithl (the proper dower for a woman of her status), the wife's word is accepted because the apparent circumstance (that she is entitled to at least mahr al-mithl) supports her. If she claims more than mahr al-mithl, then the husband's word is accepted because the apparent circumstance (that the mahr is not excessive) supports him. This application shows how the principle balances the burden of proof based on what is externally plausible.

Key Terms
قول (qaw1): Statement or claim of a party that is given legal weight in the absence of clear evidence, based on preponderant apparent circumstance.
ظاهر (zahir): The apparent circumstance or external evidence that supports one party's claim over the other. In this context, it is the known standard of mahr al-mithl.
دعوی (da'wa): A legal claim made by a party in a dispute. The principle is about which party's claim is accepted when both make claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between spouses over the mahr amount, how is the conflict resolved according to the principle 'al-qawl fi al-da'awa qawl man yashhadu lahu al-zahir'?
A) The wife's word is always accepted regardless of the amount.
B) The husband's word is always accepted.
C) The wife's word is accepted up to mahr al-mithl; beyond that, the husband's word is accepted.
D) The judge determines the mahr arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
When there is no evidence, the claim supported by apparent circumstance prevails; in mahr disputes, this yields a ruling for the wife up to the mahr al-mithl and for the husband beyond it.

Principle of Preferring the Claim Supported by Apparent Circumstance
States a legal maxim and applies it to mahr dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that the claim supported by al-zahir is preferred and apply it to resolve a mahr dispute by identifying the role of mahr al-mithl and the shift in burden of proof.

Core Idea
In disputes, the party whose claim aligns with the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) is given priority; for mahr, the wife is believed up to mahr al-mithl, the husband beyond.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi maxim for resolving conflicting claims: the word of the party whose statement is supported by the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) is accepted. This maxim is then applied to a common marital dispute over the mahr amount. Understanding this principle is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurisprudence balances fairness and practicality in judicial evidence, particularly in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general maxim
Read the opening Arabic: 'إِنَّ الْقَوْلَ فِى الدَّعَاوَى قَوْلُ مَنْ يَشْهَدُ لَهُ الظَّاهِرُ عِنْدَ الطَّرَفَيْنِ'. Understand that 'al-zahir' refers to the apparent circumstance or external evidence that points to one party's truthfulness.
This maxim is a key rule of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Define 'al-zahir' in this context
Al-zahir is the prima facie indication that shifts the burden of proof. In the mahr example, the default obligation of mahr al-mithl creates an apparent circumstance supporting the wife up to that amount, and supporting the husband beyond it.
3
Apply to the mahr dispute
The wife claims a high mahr, the husband denies. The maxim resolves this by looking to mahr al-mithl (standard mahr). Up to that amount, the apparent supports the wife (since marriage imposes at least that), so her word is accepted. For any excess, the apparent shifts to the husband, so his denial is accepted.
This is the thamarah (practical outcome) of the maxim.
4
Understand determination of mahr al-mithl
The passage explains that mahr al-mithl is assessed by looking at female paternal relatives (e.g., paternal aunts, cousins) who are similar in beauty, age, wealth, and virginity. The mother's mahr is irrelevant unless she is also from the father's lineage (e.g., a cousin).
This is unique to the Hanafi school; Shafi'is include maternal relatives as well.
5
Recognize the qiyas (analogy) to the dyer case
The maxim is supported by qiyas to a dispute between a cloth owner and a dyer over the wage: the standard wage is used. Similarly, for mahr, the standard (mahr al-mithl) is taken as the default. This confirms that when a specific amount is contested, the apparent points to a standard value.
The illa (effective cause) is the presence of a known standard value (mithl) that serves as a reference point.

وَلَكِنَّا نَقُولُ: قِيمَةُ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالرُجُوعِ إِلَى قِيمَةِ جِنْسِهِ، وَالْإِنْسَانُ مِنْ جِئْسِ قَوْمِ أَبِيهِ لَا مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمٍ أُمِّهِ، أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْأُمَّ قَدْ مِنْ قَوْمٍ أَبِيهَا بِأَنْ كَانَتْ بِنْتَ عَمِّهِ، فَحِينَئِذٍ يُعْتَبَرُ مَهْرُهَا لَا لِأَنَّهَا أُمَّهَا بَلْ، لِأَنَّهَا بِئْتُ عَمِّ أَبِيهَا، وَإِنَّمَا يُعْتَبَرُ مِنْ عَشِيرَتِهَا امْرَأَةٌ هِيَ مِثْلُهَا فِي الْحُسْنِ، وَالْجَمَالِ وَالسِّنِّ وَالْمَالِ وَالْبَكَارَةِ، لَّانَّ الْمُهُورَ تَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِ هَذِهِ الْأَوْصَافِ. المبسوط للسرخسي کتاب النکاح باب المهر، ج ۵ ص ۶۴، ط: دار المعرفة وَإِنَّمَا يُضَافُ إِلَى أَقَارِبِ الأب لأنَّ النَّسَبَ إِلَيْهِ، وَلَأنَّ قِيمَةَ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالرُّجُوعِ إِلَى قِيمَةِ جِنْسِهِ وَالْإِنْسَانُ مِنْ جِنْسِ قَوْمِ أَبِيهِ لَا قَبِيلَتِهَا) بِأَنْ يَكُونَ أَبُوهَا تَزَوَّجَ بِنْتَ عَمِّهِ فَإِنَّ أُمَّهَا وَخَالَتَهَا تَكُونُ مِنْ قَبِيلَتِهَا. وَقَوْلُهُ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا) إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ وَقِيمَةُ الشَّيْء إِنَّمَا تُعْرَفُ بِالنَّظَرِ فِي قِيمَةِ جِنسِهِ. العناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۳۶۸، ط: دار الفكر الهداية كتاب النكاح باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۶، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, the statement in claims is the statement of the one for whom the apparent circumstance testifies, according to both parties. Translation: According to the two parties, among claims, the statement of that person is accepted whose favor the apparent circumstance testifies. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that in claims, the statement of that person will be accepted for whom the apparent circumstance testifies, i.e., whose statement conforms to the apparent. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that if husband and wife differ regarding mahr, i.e., the woman claims more mahr and the husband denies this excess, then in this case, up to the completion of mahr al-mithl, the woman's statement will be accepted, and beyond mahr al-mithl, the husband's. But we say: The value of a thing is known only by referring to the value of its kind, and a person is of the kind of his father's people, not of the kind of his mother's people. Do you not see that the mother may be a slave-girl, and the daughter may be a Qurayshite, following her father. For this reason, consideration is given to her paternal relatives, and her mahr is not determined by her mother's mahr unless her mother is from her father's people, such as being his cousin; then her mahr is considered not because she is her mother but because she is her father's cousin. And only a woman from her relatives who is like her in beauty, comeliness, age, wealth, and virginity is considered, for mahr varies with these attributes. (Al-Mabsut li al-Sarakhsi, Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 5, p. 64, Dar al-Ma'rifah) And it is attributed to paternal relatives because lineage is to him, and because the value of a thing is known only by referring to the value of its kind, and a person is of the kind of his father's people, not of the kind of his mother's people; do you not see that the mother may be a slave-girl and the daughter may be a Qurayshite, following her father, and her mother and maternal aunt are not considered if they are not of her tribe, such as if her father married his cousin, then her mother and maternal aunt are of her tribe. And his statement 'for what we have explained' refers to his statement 'and the value of a thing is known only by considering the value of its kind.' (Al-Inayah, Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 3, p. 368, Dar al-Fikr; Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2, p. 356, Rahmaniyyah)
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational principle of Hanafi judicial evidence: in disputes, the party whose claim aligns with the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) is given credence. The text applies this to a common marital dispute where the wife claims a higher mahr than the husband acknowledges. The principle resolves the conflict by looking to mahr al-mithl (the standard mahr for a woman of her status) as the default obligation in marriage. Up to the amount of mahr al-mithl, the apparent circumstance supports the wife, as the basic marriage contract imposes this. Therefore her word is accepted for that portion. For any excess beyond mahr al-mithl, the apparent circumstance shifts against her, as the standard does not require more, so the husband's denial is accepted. The passage then cites extensive reasoning from al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut and other Hanafi authorities to explain how mahr al-mithl is determined: by looking to paternal relatives, not maternal, because lineage follows the father. This is illustrated with the example of a mother being a slave and the daughter being a free Qurayshite—the daughter's status follows the father. Only if the mother's family coincides with the father's (e.g., the mother is a paternal cousin) does the mother's mahr matter, but then it is because she is a paternal relative, not because of motherhood. The attributes considered in determining mahr al-mithl are beauty, age, wealth, and virginity.

Key Terms
الظاهِرُ (al-zahir): The apparent circumstance or external evidence that supports one party's claim.
مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ (mahr al-mithl): The standard dowry for a woman of similar attributes in her paternal family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wife's, because she is the claimant
B) The husband's, because the apparent circumstance supports him
C) Both parties must provide witnesses
D) The judge decides based on the woman's mother's mahr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'the claim supported by al-zahir is accepted' resolves mahr disputes by splitting the amount at the threshold of mahr al-mithl, determined by paternal female relatives.

The Denier's Statement in Mahr Disputes: Abu Yusuf vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr procedural ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Imam Abu Yusuf's and the Sahibayn's positions on whose statement is accepted in a mahr dispute, and apply the principle of 'the apparent circumstance' (zahir) to determine the ruling in a given scenario.

Core Idea
In mahr disputes, Abu Yusuf accepts the husband's oath always; the Sahibayn use mahr al-mithl as the apparent witness.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a critical intra-Hanafi disagreement. Imam Abu Yusuf applies the general procedural rule that a denier's sworn statement is accepted. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) counter that the 'apparent circumstance' (zahir al-hal) of the mahr al-mithl acts as a witness, shifting the burden differently. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists balance procedural principles with substantive legal presumptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage to find the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn. Abu Yusuf holds that the denier's (husband's) statement with an oath is always accepted. The Sahibayn hold that the statement of the one supported by the apparent circumstance (mahr al-mithl) is accepted.
The author of al-Hidayah presents Abu Yusuf's view first, then the Sahibayn's rebuttal.
2
Understand the underlying principles
Abu Yusuf relies on the general principle: 'The statement of the denier with an oath.' The Sahibayn rely on: 'The statement in claims is of the one whom the apparent circumstance supports.' Recognize that the 'apparent' here is the mahr al-mithl, the original obligation.
The difference arises from whether the existence of a known default (mahr al-mithl) creates an apparent support that modifies the burden of proof.
3
Work through an example
Assume mahr al-mithl is 1000. Wife claims 2000, husband says 1000. According to Abu Yusuf: husband's statement accepted, so he only owes 1000. According to Sahibayn: up to 1000, wife's statement is accepted (since apparent supports her), so she gets 1000; beyond that, husband's statement is accepted, so she gets only 1000 unless she proves the excess.
In this example, the practical outcome is the same (1000). But if the wife claimed 500 and husband said 1000, the Sahibayn would accept her statement up to 1000, while Abu Yusuf would accept his statement, so she gets 1000 or 500? Actually careful: If wife claims 500 (less than mahr al-mithl), then according to Sahibayn, the apparent supports her (she is not claimant of increase), so her statement is accepted. According to Abu Yusuf, the husband is denier of increase? Actually if wife claims less, the husband is not denying increase; he is claiming more. The dispute scenario here is when the wife claims an amount above mahr al-mithl. The passage says 'woman is claimant of increase', so we assume she claims more than mahr al-mithl.
4
Examine the dyer-and-cloth analogy
The Sahibayn support their view with qiyas: like a dyer and cloth owner disputing wage, the value of the dye (customary) is benchmark. Similarly, mahr al-mithl is the benchmark in marriage. This analogy illustrates that when a default value exists, it shifts the burden of proof.
The illa (effective cause) is that both involve a dispute over consideration where the default is determined by custom.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn, as indicated by the author of al-Hidayah. This means in Hanafi fatwa, the apparent circumstance of mahr al-mithl is considered.
This is an example of an intra-Hanafi dispute where the later school settled on the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۷) إِنَّ الْقَوْلَ قَوْلُ الْمُنْكِرِ مَعَ الْيَمِينِ عِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ .
ترجمہ: امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک منکر کا قول اُس کی قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہو گا۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک جب مدعی کے پاس گواہ نہ ہوں تو اس صورت میں منکر کی بات کی تصدیق مع الیمین ہوگی ، یعنی منکر کے حق میں فیصلہ یمین کے ساتھ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ مذکورہ بالا مسئلہ میں امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک چاہے یہ اختلاف طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں ہو یا طلاق بعد الدخول کی صورت میں ،شوہر ہی کے قول کا اعتبار ہوگا، اس لئے کہ عورت زیادتی کا دعوی کرتی ہے اور شوہر اس زیادتی کا منکر ہے، اور منکر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی شوہر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہو گا۔
لَّانَّ الْمَرْأَةَ مُدَّعِيَةُ لِلزِّيَادَةِ وَهُوَ يُنْكِرُهَا وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْقَوْلَ فِى الدَّعَاوَى قَوْلُ مَنْ يَشْهَدُ لَهُ الظَّاهِرُ. وَالظَّاهِرُ شَاهِدٌ لِمَنْ يَشْهَدُ لَهُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ؛ لأنَّهُ هُوَ الْمُوجِبُ الْأَصْلِيُّ فِي بَابِ النِّكَاحِ وَصَارَ كَالصَّبَّاغِ مَعَ رَبِّ الثَّوْبِ إِذَا اخْتَلَفَا فِي مِقْدَارِ الْأَجْرِ تُحَكِّمُ قِيمَةُ الصَّبْغِ.
البحر الرائق: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۱۹۳ ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي الهداية كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۶، ط: رحمانیه
الأبي يوسف أن المرأة قد تدعى الزيادة، والزوج ينكر، والقول قول المنكر مع يمينه، إلا أن يأتى بشيء يكذبه الظاهر فيه بأن ذكر أقل من عشرة دراهم؛ لأن ظاهر الشرع ينكره وظاهر الحال يكذبه.
البناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۵ ص ۱۹۲، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
Principle 27: Indeed, the statement is the statement of the denier with the oath according to Abu Yusuf. Translation: According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the statement of the denier will be considered valid along with his oath. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, when the claimant has no witnesses, then in that case the word of the denier is confirmed with the oath, meaning the verdict will be in favor of the denier with the oath. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that in the aforementioned issue, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, whether this dispute is in the case of divorce before consummation or in the case of divorce after consummation, only the husband's statement will be considered, because the woman claims an increase and the husband denies that increase, and the denier's statement with oath is considered, so here too the husband's statement with oath will be considered. Because the woman is the claimant of the increase and he denies it, and for them (the two, i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the statement in claims is the statement of the one whom the apparent circumstance supports. And the apparent circumstance is a witness for one whom the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) supports; because it is the original obligation in marriage and it becomes like the dyer with the owner of the garment when they dispute over the amount of the wage, the value of the dye is taken as a benchmark. (References from al-Bahr al-Raiq, al-Hidayah, al-Binaya)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whose word is accepted in a dispute over mahr (dower) between husband and wife. The author presents a principle (qaida) from Imam Abu Yusuf: 'The statement is the statement of the denier with an oath.' This means in the absence of witnesses, the defendant's sworn word is taken. The author explains that in the specific case of a mahr dispute—whether before or after consummation—Abu Yusuf holds that the husband's word is accepted because he denies the wife's claim of a higher dower. The wife is the claimant of an increase, and the husband is the denier. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree. Their principle is: 'The statement in claims is of the one whom the apparent circumstance (zahir) supports.' Here, the apparent circumstance is the proper dower (mahr al-mithl), which is the original obligation in marriage. So, whichever party's claim aligns with mahr al-mithl, that party has the apparent supporting them. The author then gives an analogy: like a dispute between a dyer and a cloth owner over the wage, where the value of the dye is the benchmark. The passage references al-Hidayah and other works.

Key Terms
منكر (munkir): The denier; the party who denies the claim of the other.
مدعي (mudda'i): The claimant; the party who asserts a right or increase.
يمين (yamin): Oath; a sworn statement taken from the denier to confirm his denial.
ظاهر (zahir): Apparent circumstance; the external state of affairs that is presumed to be true until proven otherwise.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower; the amount of dower customary for a woman of similar status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, whose statement is accepted when the spouses dispute over the mahr amount and neither has witnesses?
A) The wife's, because she is the claimant
B) The husband's, because he is the denier
C) The judges' discretion
D) The witness of mahr al-mithl

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the rule 'the denier's statement is accepted with an oath' is qualified by the apparent circumstance, so in mahr disputes the mahr al-mithl determines whose word prevails.

Accepting Testimony Contradicting the Apparent
States the principle that evidence contradicting the apparent is accepted, and applies it to mahr disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-bayyinah khilaf al-zahir tuqbal' to identify the claimant in a mahr dispute and determine whose evidence is accepted.

Core Idea
Evidence that contradicts the default presumption identifies the claimant, and that claimant's evidence is always accepted.

In legal disputes, the default state or apparent circumstance (zahir) is taken as the baseline. Any party whose evidence contradicts this baseline is the claimant (mudda'i), and Hanafi law grants their evidence priority. This lesson unpacks the maxim 'Whose evidence is contrary to the apparent, his evidence is accepted' as applied in the Hidayah to mahr disputes, showing how the same rule governs both high and low mahr claims.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Read the maxim carefully: 'Whose evidence is contrary to the apparent, his evidence is accepted.' Understand that this is a procedural rule of evidence.
The maxim identifies the claimant.
2
Identify the claimant
The party whose witnesses contradict the apparent is the claimant. In a mahr dispute, the apparent is the mahr al-mithl (the proper dower). If the wife claims a higher amount, she is the claimant; if the husband claims a lower amount, he is the claimant.
3
Apply to first scenario
When mahr al-mithl is 1000 or less, and the wife claims 2000, her witnesses contradict the apparent (they claim more than the default), so they are accepted.
The wife is the claimant.
4
Apply to second scenario
When mahr al-mithl is 2000 or more, and the husband claims 1000, his witnesses contradict the apparent (they claim less than the default), so they are accepted.
The husband is the claimant.
5
Generalize
This principle applies to any case where one party's evidence goes against the default presumption. The rule ensures that the party who challenges the status quo must bring evidence, and that evidence is given weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۸) مَنْ كَانَتْ بَيِّنَةُ خِلَافِ الظَّاهِرِ تُقْبَلُ بَيْنَتُهُ.
ترجمہ: جس کے گواہ ظاہر کے خلاف ہوں تو اس کے گواہ مقبول ہوں گے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس آدمی کے گواہ ظاہر کے خلاف ہوں تو اُن کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی ، اس لئے جس کے گواہ خلاف ظاہر ہوں گے وہ مدعی ہوگا اور مدعی کا بینہ قبول ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ مذکورہ بالا مسئلہ کی پہلی صورت میں یعنی جب مہر مثل ایک ہزار ہو یا ایک ہزار سے کم ہو اور بیوی دو ہزار کا دعوی کرتی ہو ، اور دونوں میاں بیوی نے گواہ بھی پیش کر دیئے تو عورت کے گواہ قبول کئے جائیں گے، کیونکہ جب مہر مثل ایک ہزار یا اس سے کم ہو اور گواہ دو ہزار کی گواہی دیں تو یہ خلاف ظاہر کی گواہی دے رہے ہیں اور جس کے گواہ ظاہر کے خلاف ہوں وہ مقبول ہوتے ہیں، لہذا پہلی صورت میں عورت کے گواہ مقبول ہوں گے اور دوسری صورت میں یعنی جب مہر مثل دو ہزار یا زیادہ ہو اور شوہر ہزار کا دعوی کرتا ہو تو شوہر کے گواہ مقبول ہوں گے ، وجہ وہی ہے جو ابھی گزری ہے۔
الهداية كتاب النكاح باب المهر، ج ٢ ص 356، ط: رحمانیه
(وَأَيُّهُمَا أَقَامَ الْبَيِّنَةَ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ) أَى فِيمَا إِذَا شَهِدَ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ لِلزَّوْجِ وَفِيمَا إِذَا شَهِدَ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ لِلْمَرْأَةِ تُقْبَلُ، وَإِنْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ فِى الْوَجْهِ الْأَوَّلِ) وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا كَتانَ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ شَاهِدًا لِلزَّوْج (تُقْبَلُ بَيْنَتُهَا لِأَنَّهَا تُثْبِتُ الزَّيَادَةَ وَفِي الْوَجْهِ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا كَانَ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ شَاهِدًا لِلْمَرْأَةِ تُقْبَلُ بَيِّنَتُهُ لِأَنَّهَا تُثبتُ الْحَطَّ وَالأصْلُ فِى هَذَا أَنَّ الْبَيِّنَةَ تُثْبِتُ مَا لَيْسَ بِثَابِتٍ ظَاهِرًا.
Principle 28: Whose evidence is contrary to the apparent, his evidence is accepted. Translation: Whose witnesses are contrary to the apparent, his witnesses will be accepted. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if a person's witnesses are contrary to the apparent, their testimony will be accepted, because the one whose witnesses are contrary to the apparent is the claimant, and the claimant's evidence is accepted. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that in the first scenario of the aforementioned issue, i.e., when the proper dower is one thousand or less and the wife claims two thousand, and both spouses have produced witnesses, then the wife's witnesses will be accepted. Because when the proper dower is one thousand or less and the witnesses testify to two thousand, they are testifying contrary to the apparent, and whose witnesses are contrary to the apparent, they are accepted. So in the first scenario, the wife's witnesses are accepted. In the second scenario, i.e., when the proper dower is two thousand or more and the husband claims one thousand, then the husband's witnesses are accepted, for the same reason already given. (Reference from al-Hidayah: Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr, and quote explaining that whichever of them establishes evidence in the two situations is accepted, etc.)
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim (qaida): 'Whose evidence is contrary to the apparent, his evidence is accepted.' The author explains that this is because a person whose witnesses contradict the apparent state of affairs is necessarily the claimant (mudda'i), and the claimant's evidence is admissible. The principle is then applied to the mahr dispute discussed earlier. In the first scenario, where mahr al-mithl is 1000 or less and the wife claims 2000, her witnesses are testifying to an amount beyond the obvious (contrary to zahir), so they are accepted. In the second scenario, where mahr al-mithl is 2000 or more and the husband claims 1000, his witnesses contradict the apparent (by claiming less), so they are accepted. The passage then quotes al-Hidayah, elaborating that the basic rule is that evidence establishes what is not already established by the apparent.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, specifically the testimony of witnesses in a legal dispute.
خلاف الظاهر (khilaf al-zahir): Contrary to the apparent circumstance; evidence that contradicts the default state or presumption.
مدعي (mudda'i): Claimant; the party who asserts something contrary to the apparent state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband's, because he denies the increase
B) The wife's, because her witnesses contradict the apparent
C) Neither, because both have evidence
D) The witnesses are not needed

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Whose evidence is contrary to the apparent, his evidence is accepted' is a fundamental procedural rule in Hanafi law that identifies the claimant and accepts their evidence in mahr disputes.

Mahr al-Mithl as the Original Obligation in Marriage
States that mahr al-mithl is the default obligation according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that mahr al-mithl is the original obligation in marriage and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is the default obligation even when a specific dower is named.

In the Hanafi school, a foundational principle governs disputes about the dower (mahr) in marriage. While the contract may specify an amount, the school's leading imams—Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani—hold that the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is the original obligation. This means that when the dower is disputed or invalid, the default is the amount customary for a woman of similar status. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagreed, creating an intra-Hanafi difference that affects how such disputes are resolved in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Recognize that the passage states a legal maxim: mahr al-mithl is the original obligation (al-muujib al-asli) in the chapter of marriage according to al-tarafaan (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
The term 'original obligation' means the default legal requirement when no valid specific dower exists.
2
Understand the disagreement
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf holds a contrary view. He considers the named dower as the primary obligation, not mahr al-mithl. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Intra-Hanafi disputes are common; the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is usually that of the majority (the two).
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a dispute over dower, according to the two, the wife's claim up to mahr al-mithl is upheld unless the husband can prove a lesser amount; according to Abu Yusuf, the husband's denial under oath is accepted at face value.
This difference affects judicial decisions in marriage dower disputes.
4
Determine the tarjih
The author of al-Hidayah indicates that the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
The tarjih mechanism in al-Hidayah often favors the majority of the school founders.

Source Text

ترجمہ: نکاح کے باب میں طرفین کے نزدیک مہر مثل ہی موجب اصلی ہے، امام ابو یوسف کا اس میں اختلاف ہے۔
