العناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۳۷۶، ط: دار الفکر
الهداية كتاب النكاح باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۶، ط: رحمانیه
Principle 29: Indeed, the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is the original obligation in the chapter of marriage according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. Translation: In the chapter of marriage, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), mahr al-mithl is the original obligation; Imam Abu Yusuf differs on this. (References from al-Hidayah, al-Inayah, al-Hidayah)
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (intra_hanafi_dispute) concerning the primary obligation in the marriage contract regarding dower. It states that according to the 'two' (at-tarafayn)—meaning Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani—the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is the original obligation (muujib asli). This means that in determining the dower, the default benchmark is the customary dower for a woman of similar status, not the amount named in the contract if disputed. Imam Abu Yusuf holds a contrary opinion. The practical effect of this difference is seen in disputes over mahr, as discussed in the previous principles. The passage provides references to al-Hidayah and al-Inayah.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower; the amount customary for a woman of similar status, family, and beauty.
موجب أصلي (muujib asli): The original obligation; the default legal requirement in the contract.
الطرفان (at-tarafaan): The two: referring to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The dower named in the contract
B) The proper dower (mahr al-mithl)
C) Half the named dower
D) No dower is obligatory

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is the default dower obligation in Hanafi fiqh per the majority of the school founders, forming the basis for dispute resolution.

Nikah — Marriage

Mahr al-Mithl vs. Mahr Musamma: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Original Obligator
Intra-Hanafi dispute resolution via composite consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the original obligator for mahr and explain how the dispute results in composite consensus (ijmaʿ murakkab) when specification is contested.

Core Idea
Two Hanafi positions on mahr yield the same ruling via composite consensus.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute: is the proper dowry (mahr al-mithl) the primary basis in marriage, or is it the specified dowry (mahr musamma)? While Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that mahr al-mithl is the original obligator, Imam Abu Yusuf considers mahr musamma to be primary. Remarkably, when spouses disagree on whether a mahr was specified at all, both positions lead to the same practical ruling: mahr al-mithl is wajib. This phenomenon is called composite consensus (ijmaʿ murakkab), a key concept in Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
State the core dispute
Identify the two positions: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, mahr al-mithl is the original obligator (mujib asli). According to Abu Yusuf, mahr musamma is the original obligator.
The phrase 'inda al-tarafayn refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
2
Understand each position's rationale
For Abu Hanifa/Muhammad: the default in marriage is that mahr al-mithl applies; mahr musamma is an exception that temporarily overrides it. For Abu Yusuf: parties usually specify a mahr, so mahr musamma is the default; mahr al-mithl is a fallback when specification fails.
These are two different views on which factor primarily triggers the obligation.
3
Identify the contested scenario
The scenario where spouses disagree on whether mahr was specified at all (aṣl al-musammā). Because the proof of specification is absent or conflicting, the specification cannot be established.
This is the case where both parties claim opposite specifications or one denies any specification.
4
Trace the outcome from each position
From Abu Hanifa/Muhammad: mahr al-mithl applies directly. From Abu Yusuf: since mahr musamma is impossible to determine, resort is made to mahr al-mithl. Both end at mahr al-mithl.
The result is unanimous, though the path differs.
5
Define composite consensus (ijmaʿ murakkab)
An agreement on the ruling despite disagreement on the underlying principle. Here, all three imams agree that mahr al-mithl is wajib in this scenario, forming a binding consensus.
This consensus gives the ruling additional authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ: نکاح کے باب میں طرفین کے نزدیک مہر مثل ہی موجب اصلی ہے، امام ابو یوسف کا اس میں اختلاف ہے۔
الهداية كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۶، ۳۵۷، ط: رحمانیه (وَأَيُّهُمَا أَقَامَ الْبَيِّنَةَ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ) أَى فِيمَا إِذَا شَهِدَ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ لِلزَّوْجِ وَفِيمَا إِذَا شَهِدَ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ لِلْمَرْأَةِ تُقْبَلُ، وَإِنْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ فِى الْوَجْهِ الْأَوَّلِ) وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا كَارَتْ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ شَاهِدًا لِلزَّوْج (تُقْبَلُ بَيْنَتُهَا لِأَنَّهَا تُثْبِتُ الزَّيَادَةَ وَفِي الْوَجْهِ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا كَانَ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ شَاهِدًا لِلْمَرْأَةِ تُقْبَلُ بَيِّنَتُهُ لِأَنَّهَا تُثبتُ الْحَطَّ وَالأصْلُ فِى هَذَا أَنَّ الْبَيِّنَةَ تُثْبِتُ مَا لَيْسَ بِثَابِتٍ ظَاهِرًا.
العناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۳۷۶، ط: دار الفکر

اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی

تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک نکاح کے باب میں موجبِ اصلی مہر مثل ہے یعنی جب مہر مثل پر فیصلہ متعذر ہو اس وقت مہر سمی واجب ہوتا ہے جبکہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک مہر سمی موجب اصلی ہے یعنی جب مہر سمی متعذر ہو جائے اس وقت مہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کرتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر میاں بیوی کا اصل مسمی میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو اس صورت میں بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ طرفین کے نزدیک تو اس لئے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا کہ ان کے نزدیک باب نکاح میں موجب اصلی مہر مثل ہی ہے اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک اس لئے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا کہ ان کے نزدیک جب مہر سمی متعذر ہو جائے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوتا ہے اور یہاں بھی چونکہ مہرسمی پر فیصلہ کر نامتعذر رہے لہذا مہر مثل ہی واجب ہوگا۔
Indeed, mahr al-mithl (proper dowry) is the original obligator in the chapter of marriage according to the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. Translation: In the chapter of marriage, according to the two parties, mahr al-mithl is the original obligator. Imam Abu Yusuf differs on this. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2, p. 356-357, Rahmaniyya ed. (and whichever of the two establishes evidence in the two ways) i.e., in the case where mahr al-mithl testifies for the husband and in the case where mahr al-mithl testifies for the woman, it is accepted. And if both present evidence in the first case—that is, when mahr al-mithl testifies for the husband—her evidence is accepted because it proves the increase. And in the second case—that is, when mahr al-mithl testifies for the woman—his evidence is accepted because it proves the decrease. The principle in this is that evidence establishes what is not apparently established. Al-Inayah, Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 3, p. 376, Dar al-Fikr. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2, p. 356, Rahmaniyya ed. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that according to the two parties, the original obligator in the chapter of marriage is mahr al-mithl, meaning that when judgment by mahr al-mithl is possible, mahr musamma becomes obligatory. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, mahr musamma is the original obligator, i.e., when mahr musamma is impossible to implement, then one resorts to mahr al-mithl. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if the husband and wife have a disagreement over the original specification (aṣl al-musammā), then in this case, with combined consensus (ijmāʿ murakkab), mahr al-mithl will be obligatory. Because for the two parties, mahr al-mithl will be obligatory since, in their view, mahr al-mithl is the original obligator in the chapter of marriage. And for Imam Abu Yusuf, mahr al-mithl will be obligatory because, in his view, when mahr musamma is impossible to implement, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory, and here, since judgment by mahr musamma is impossible due to lack of proof of specification, mahr al-mithl will be obligatory.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafī dispute on the role of mahr al-mithl (proper dowry) in marriage. The Arabic text states a principle: 'Mahr al-mithl is the original obligator (mūjib aṣlī) in the chapter of marriage according to both parties (al-ṭarafayn—referring to Imām Abū Ḥanīfah and Imām Muḥammad), contrary to Abū Yūsuf.' The Urdu commentary explains that for the two (Abū Ḥanīfah and Muḥammad), mahr al-mithl is the primary basis, and mahr musamma (specified dowry) becomes due only when mahr al-mithl cannot be applied. For Abū Yūsuf, the opposite is true: mahr musamma is primary, and one resorts to mahr al-mithl only when mahr musamma cannot be implemented. The author of Al-Hidayah then clarifies the practical result: when spouses disagree on whether mahr was specified at all (aṣl al-musammā), both positions lead to the same outcome—mahr al-mithl is obligatory. For the two, it is directly because mahr al-mithl is the origin. For Abū Yūsuf, it is because mahr musamma cannot be fixed due to the dispute, so mahr al-mithl becomes necessary. This is called 'composite consensus' (ijmāʿ murakkab): although the reasoning differs, the ruling is unanimous. The passage emphasizes that the dispute is theoretical but yields the same result in this scenario.

Key Terms
مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ (mahr al-mithl): Proper dowry, the amount determined by the custom of women similar to the bride (e.g., paternal aunts or peers). It becomes obligatory when no mahr is specified or the specification is invalid/disputed.
مُوجِبٌ أَصْلِيٌّ (mūjib aṣlī): The original or primary basis that makes a legal obligation arise. Here, it refers to the factor that primarily determines the obligatory dower.
إِجْمَاعٌ مُرَكَّبٌ (ijmāʿ murakkab): Composite consensus: an agreement on the ruling despite differing legal reasoning or bases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Mahr al-mithl is obligatory due to composite consensus.
C) The mahr is suspended until the dispute is resolved.
D) No mahr is due because the marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the original obligator for mahr resolves into composite consensus when specification is contested, establishing mahr al-mithl as wajib.

Mahr al-Mithl After Death: Imam vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr al-mithl after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's position that mahr al-mithl has no effect after the death of both spouses and explain the disagreement of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
After both spouses die, mahr al-mithl is void according to Imam; Sahibayn say it remains a debt.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement about the persistence of mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) after both spouses die. While the obligation of mahr generally arises at marriage, the question here is whether death extinguishes the claim for mahr al-mithl when the mahr was never specified. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school treats unresolved mahr obligations in inheritance contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The precise question: does mahr al-mithl have any legal force after the death of both spouses? This arises when the mahr was not specified or the specification is disputed.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that once both spouses die, mahr al-mithl has no effect. The marriage is over and the estate is distributed by inheritance rules; no separate mahr claim survives.
This is the mufta bihi position in the school.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that mahr al-mithl remains effective after death as a debt on the estate of the deceased spouse.
They consider the obligation of mahr to survive death.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the wife dies before mahr is settled, according to Imam her heirs cannot claim mahr al-mithl; according to Sahibayn they can. This affects how inheritance is calculated.
The dispute changes the financial obligations on the estate.
5
Recognize the authority weight
Imam's view is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon for fatwa. The text of al-Hidayah gives it priority by stating 'indahu' (according to him).
This is a standard intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved in favour of Imam.

(۳۰) إِنَّهُ لَا حُكْمَ لِمَهْرِ الْمِثْلِ عِنْدَهُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِمَا خِلَافًا لَهُمَا.
ترجمہ: مہر مثل کا کوئی حکم نہیں ہے زوجین کے مرنے کے بعد امام صاحب کے نزدیک، صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب میاں بیوی مرجائیں تو ان کی وفات کے بعد امام صاحب کے نزدیک مہر مثل کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا، جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک بعد الوفاۃ بھی مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر میاں بیوی مر جائیں جبکہ اس (وَلَوْ كَانَ الاخْتِلَافُ فِى أَصْل الْمُسَمَّى بأن ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا الرَّسُمِيَةَ وَأَنْكَرَ الْآخَرُ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَ مَنْ يُنْكِرُ التَّسْمِيَةَ وَيَجِبُ مَهُرُ الْمِثْلِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ الْمُرَكَّبِ، أَمَّا عِنْدَهُمَا فَأَنَّهُ الْأَصْلُ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ، وَأَمَّا عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ فَلَانَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ الْقَضَاء بِالْمُسَمَّى لِعَدَمِ ثُبُوتِ التَّسْمِيَةِ للاختلافِ فَيَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ كَمَا لَوْ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَلَمْ يُسَمِّ لَهَا مَهْرًا.
العناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۳۷۷، ط: دار الفکر
الهداية كتاب النكاح باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۷، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, there is no ruling (effect) for mahr al-mithl according to him (Imam Abu Hanifa) after the death of both, contrary to them (the two Sahibayn). Translation: There is no effect of mahr al-mithl after the death of the spouses according to Imam, and the Sahibayn differ. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when the spouses die, after their death, according to Imam, mahr al-mithl will have no consideration, while according to the Sahibayn, after death, mahr al-mithl will still be considered. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if the spouses die while there is a dispute over the original specification (aṣl al-musammā) – as when one claims specification and the other denies it – the statement of the one who denies the specification is accepted, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory by composite consensus. As for the two (Sahibayn), it is because the principle in arbitration is mahr al-mithl. As for Abu Yusuf, it is because judgment by the specified mahr is impossible due to lack of proof of specification due to the dispute, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory just as if he married her without specifying a dower.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage addresses another intra-Hanafī disagreement: after both spouses die, does mahr al-mithl have any legal effect? Imām Abū Ḥanīfah holds that it has no effect; once both are dead, the issue of mahr is moot because the heirs inherit the estate based on other rules. The Two Companions (Ṣāḥibayn), Imām Abū Yūsuf and Imām Muḥammad, disagree and hold that mahr al-mithl is still relevant even after death. The author of Al-Hidayah applies this principle to a scenario that extends the previous dispute: if the spouses die while they had a disagreement over whether a mahr was actually specified (aṣl al-musammā), the rule remains that the one who denies specification is believed (because the default is no specification), and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. However, this is by composite consensus only during their lifetime. After death, the disagreement surfaces: Imām says no mahr al-mithl is due because death extinguishes the need for the mahr ruling (the marriage is over and heirs take fixed shares). The Ṣāḥibayn say it is still due because the obligation of mahr survives death as a debt on the deceased's estate. The commentary notes that Abū Yūsuf's reasoning aligns with his view that mahr musamma is primary, but when specification is not proven, mahr al-mithl becomes a debt. The practical difference: if the wife dies first, her heirs might claim mahr al-mithl; if the husband dies first, the wife's claim for mahr remains. The dispute affects whether her heirs can inherit that mahr.

Key Terms
حُكْم (ḥukm): Legal effect or ruling; here it means the legal enforceability or consideration of mahr al-mithl after death.
صَاحِبَين (ṣāḥibayn): The two companions: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two major students of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens to the claim for mahr al-mithl if both spouses die before settling the mahr?
A) The claim remains valid and must be paid from the estate.
B) The claim becomes void and no mahr is due.
C) Only the husband's heirs must pay.
D) The court determines mahr al-mithl regardless.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi view is that mahr al-mithl has no legal effect after both spouses die, contrary to the opinion of the Sahibayn.

Dispute over Mahr Specification: Original Cause and Mahr al-Mithl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the original cause of mahr and compound consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that mahr al-mithl becomes wajib when the specification of mahr is disputed, and identify the compound consensus (ijma' murakkab) underlying the ruling.

Core Idea
When mahr specification is disputed, denial is believed, making mahr al-mithl obligatory by compound consensus of the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the foundational principle (mujib) of mahr in marriage. While the Sahibayn consider mahr al-mithl as the original cause, Abu Yusuf holds mahr musamma as primary. Yet both agree on the ruling when a dispute arises over whether any mahr was specified. Understanding this compound consensus (ijma' murakkab) is essential to grasp how Hanafi jurists reconcile different usul to produce a uniform ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The case: husband and wife disagree over whether a mahr was specified at all (asl al-musamma). One claims specification, the other denies it.
This is a dispute over the existence of any specified mahr, not over the amount.
2
Apply the default procedural rule
The one denying specification is believed (al-qawl li al-munkir), because the burden of proof is on the claimant.
This is a standard rule in cases of denial.
3
Understand compound consensus
Both Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam Abu Yusuf agree that mahr al-mithl becomes wajib, but for different reasons. This is ijma' murakkab: same result, different istidlal.
Ijma' murakkab is a type of consensus where the hukm is agreed upon but the proofs differ.
4
Analyze the reasoning of the Sahibayn
According to the Sahibayn, mahr al-mithl is the original cause (mujib) in marriage. Since no specified mahr is established, the default mahr al-mithl applies directly.
For them, mahr musamma is exceptional; mahr al-mithl is the rule.
5
Analyze the reasoning of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that mahr musamma is the original cause. However, when it is impossible to enforce due to lack of proof (the dispute prevents verification), the default shifts to mahr al-mithl, similar to a marriage with no specification.
This is a fallback mechanism, not the primary rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک نکاح کے باب میں موجبِ اصلی مہر مثل ہے یعنی جب مہر مثل پر فیصلہ متعذر ہو اس وقت مہر سمی واجب ہوتا ہے جبکہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک مہر سمی موجب اصلی ہے یعنی جب مہر سمی متعذ رہو جائے اس وقت مہر مثل کی طرف رجوع کرتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر میاں بیوی کا اصل مسمی میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو اس صورت میں بالا جماع مہر مثل واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ طرفین کے نزدیک تو اس لئے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا کہ ان کے نزدیک باب نکاح میں موجب اصلی مہر مثل ہی ہے اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک اس لئے مہر مثل واجب ہوگا کہ ان کے نزدیک جب مہر سمی متعذر ہو جائے تو مہر مثل واجب ہوتا ہے اور یہاں بھی چونکہ مہرسمی پر فیصلہ کر نامتعذ رہے لہذا مہر مثل ہی واجب ہوگا۔
(وَلَوْ كَانَ الاخْتِلَافُ فِى أَصْل الْمُسَمَّى بأن ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا التَّسْمِيَةَ وَأَنْكَرَ الْآخَرُ كَانَ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَ مَنْ يُنْكِرُ التَّسْمِيَةَ وَيَجِبُ مَهُرُ الْمِثْلِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ الْمُرَكَّبِ، أَمَّا عِنْدَهُمَا فَأَنَّهُ الْأَصْلُ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ، وَأَمَّا عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ فَلِأَنَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ الْقَضَاء بِالْمُسَمَّى لِعَدَمِ ثُبُوتِ التَّسْمِيَةِ للاختلافِ فَيَجِبُ مَهْرُ الْمِثْلِ كَمَا لَوْ تَزَوَّجَهَا وَلَمْ يُسَمِّ لَهَا مَهْرًا.) العناية: كتاب النكاح، باب المهر، ج ۳ ص ۳۷۷، ط: دار الفکر الهداية كتاب النكاح باب المهر، ج ۲ ص ۳۵۷، ط: رحمانیه
Usool E Hidayah Volume 2 Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that according to the two parties (Sahibayn), the original cause in the chapter of marriage is mahr al-mithl, i.e., when judgment on mahr al-mithl becomes impossible, then mahr musamma becomes obligatory; whereas according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), mahr musamma is the original cause, i.e., when mahr musamma becomes impossible, then one turns to mahr al-mithl. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle and is informing that if the husband and wife dispute over the original specification (asl al-musamma), then in that case, by consensus, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory, because according to the two parties, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory because in their view, in the chapter of marriage, the original cause is mahr al-mithl; and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory because in his view, when mahr musamma becomes impossible, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory, and here also, since judgment on mahr musamma is impossible, therefore mahr al-mithl will be obligatory.
(And if the dispute is concerning the original specification, such that one of them claims specification and the other denies it, then the statement of the one who denies specification is believed, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory by compound consensus. As for according to the two (Sahibayn), it is because it (mahr al-mithl) is the original for arbitration; and as for according to Abu Yusuf, it is because judgment by the specified (mahr) becomes impossible due to the lack of proof of specification because of the dispute, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory, just as if he married her and did not specify a mahr for her.) Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 3 p. 377, Dar al-Fikr; Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Nikah, Bab al-Mahr, vol. 2 p. 357, Rahmaniyya.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the underlying principle (usool) of mahr in the chapter of marriage. The author of Hidayah explains a legal principle: according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, known as Sahibayn), the original cause (mujib) that triggers mahr is mahr al-mithl (proper dower). This means when a marriage contract is made without specification of mahr, or when specification fails, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl by default. In contrast, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the original cause is mahr musamma (specified dower), meaning the specified amount is the primary obligation, and only when that is impossible (e.g., due to dispute or lack of proof) is mahr al-mithl substituted.

The passage then applies this principle to a specific case: if the husband and wife dispute over whether a mahr was specified at all (asl al-musamma), for example, one claims a mahr was specified and the other denies it. In such a case, the one denying specification is believed (their word is taken), and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. This ruling is supported by 'ijma' murakkab' (compound consensus), meaning that although the reasons differ, both parties agree on the outcome.

The reasoning: According to the Sahibayn, mahr al-mithl is the original cause in marriage, so in any absence of established specification, mahr al-mithl applies. According to Abu Yusuf, since the specified mahr is not proven due to the dispute (the denial prevents establishment), judgment by the specified mahr becomes impossible, so the default of mahr al-mithl applies, analogous to a marriage where no mahr was specified at all.

Thus, the practical outcome is the same, but the legal reasoning differs. This illustrates a key feature of Hanafi fiqh: multiple imams can arrive at the same ruling through different usul (principles).

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to what women of similar status (family, beauty, wealth, etc.) receive in marriage.
مهر سمی (mahr musamma): The dower specifically agreed upon and mentioned in the marriage contract.
اجماع مركب (ijma' murakkab): Compound consensus where scholars agree on the same ruling but derive it from different principles or proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband and wife dispute over whether a mahr was specified, who is believed?
A) The one who claims specification
B) The one who denies specification
C) Both equally
D) It depends on evidence

Key Takeaway
When mahr specification is disputed, the denier is believed and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib by compound consensus, even though the Sahibayn and Abu Yusuf disagree on the underlying principle.

Mahr al-Mithl After Both Spouses Die: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Establishes the ruling on mahr al-mithl when both spouses die without specified mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on mahr al-mithl after both spouses die, explain the qiyas and istihsan used, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
After both spouses die, Abu Hanifa denies mahr al-mithl; Sahibayn affirm it as a debt.

This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on whether mahr al-mithl (proper dower) remains payable from the husband's estate when both spouses die without a specified mahr. The Sahibayn apply qiyas to treat it like specified mahr, while Abu Hanifa overrides with istihsan. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi imams balance analogy and juristic preference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two views: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that after both die, mahr al-mithl has no legal effect (heirs get nothing). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that mahr al-mithl is a debt and must be paid from the husband's estate.
The difference applies only when no mahr was specified. Specified mahr is payable by agreement.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof (qiyas)
The Sahibayn analogize mahr al-mithl to specified mahr: both become a debt (dayn) in the husband's liability upon marriage. Since specified mahr does not drop by death, mahr al-mithl likewise remains payable.
They use the 'illa of being a debt in the husband's liability.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response (istihsan)
Abu Hanifa acknowledges the qiyas but sets it aside by istihsan. He considers that mahr al-mithl is established only during the marriage; when both spouses die, the marriage ends, and the basis for mahr al-mithl ceases.
Istihsan overrides qiyas when a stronger legal consideration exists.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
When both die without a specified mahr, according to Abu Hanifa the wife's heirs receive nothing from the husband's estate. According to the Sahibayn, they receive mahr al-mithl.
The ruling also depends on order of death; if wife dies first, her right drops.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities have preferred the Sahibayn's view for fatwa, considering it more just. The mufta bihi is that mahr al-mithl is payable even after both die.
This does not weaken Abu Hanifa's view; it remains part of the school's wealth of opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٣٠) إِنَّهُ لَا حُكْمَ لِمَهرِ الْمِثْلِ عِنْدَهُ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِمَا خِلَافًا لَهُمَا. ترجمہ: مہر مثل کا کوئی حکم نہیں ہے زوجین کے مرنے کے بعد امام صاحب کے نزدیک، صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب میاں بیوی مرجائیں تو ان کی وفات کے بعد امام صاحب کے نزدیک مہر مثل کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا، جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک بعد الوفاۃ بھی مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر میاں بیوی مر جائیں جبکہ اس عورت کے لئے مہر مقرر کیا تھا تو اس صورت میں عورت کے ورثاء کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ شوہر کی میراث میں سے اس عورت کا مہر وصول کریں اور اگر عورت کے لئے مہر مقرر نہیں کیا تھا تو اس صورت میں عورت کے ورثاء کے لئے امام صاحب کے نزدیک کچھ بھی نہیں ہو گا جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں مہر مثل ہوگا، کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک زوجین کی وفات کے بعد مہر مثل کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہوتا، لہذا یہاں بھی بعد الوفاۃ مہر مثل کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ بعد وفاة الزوجین مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہوگا اور عورت کے ورثہ شوہر کے ترکہ سے اس عورت کا مہر مثل وصول کریں گے۔
(وَإِذَا مَاتَ الزَّوْجَانِ وَقَدْ سَمَّى لَهَا مَهْرًا فَلِوَرَثَتِهَا أَنْ يَأْخُذُوا ذَلِكَ مِنْ مِيرَاثِ الزَّوْجِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ سَمَّى لَهَا مَهْرًا فَلَا شَيْء لِوَرَثَتِهَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَا: لِوَرَثَتِهَا الْمَهُرُ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ مَعْنَاهُ) أَيْ مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ لِوَرَثَتِهَا الْمَهْرُ فِى الْوَجْهَيْنِ الْمُسَمَّى فِى الْوَجْهِ الْأَوَّلِ وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا سَمَّى (وَمَهُرُ الْمِثْلِ فِى الْوَجْهِ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا لَمْ يُسَمٌ (أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ) وَهُوَ وُجُوبُ الْمُسَمَّى (فَلِأَنَّ الْمُسَمَّى دَيْنٌ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ إِمَّا بِقُبُوتِهِ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ أَوْ بِالتَّصَادِقِ وَقَدْ تَأَكَّدَ بِالْمَوْتِ فَيُقْضَى مِنْ تَرِكَتِهِ) إِذَا عُلِمَ أَنَّهُمَا مَاتَا مَعًا أَوْ لَمْ يُعْلَمُ أَيُّهُمَا مَاتَ أَوَّلًا أَوْ عُلِمَ أَنَّ الزَّوْجَ مَاتَ أَوَّلًا، وَأَمَّا إِذَا عُلِمَ أَنَّهَا مَاتَتْ أَوَّلًا فَيَسْقُطُ نَصِيبُهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي فَوَجُهُ قَوْلِهِمَا أَنَّ مَهْرَ الْمِثْلِ صَارَ دَيْنًا فِي ذِمَّتِهِ كَالْمُسَمَّى فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِالْمَوْتِ كَمَا إِذَا مَاتَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَهُوَ قِيَاسُ قَوْلِهِ لَكِنُ اسْتَحْسَنَ .
(30) Indeed, there is no ruling for mahr al-mithl according to him (Abu Hanifa) after their (both spouses') death, contrary to the two (Sahibayn).
Translation: There is no ruling for mahr al-mithl after the death of the spouses according to Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him); the two companions differ.
Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when the husband and wife die, after their death, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, mahr al-mithl will not be considered, whereas according to the two companions, after death as well, mahr al-mithl will be considered. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle and is informing that if the husband and wife die, while if a mahr had been specified for the woman, then in that case the woman's heirs have the option to take that mahr from the inheritance of the husband; and if a mahr had not been specified for the woman, then in that case the woman's heirs get nothing according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while according to the two companions, in that case mahr al-mithl will be (paid). Because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, after the death of the spouses, mahr al-mithl has no consideration, therefore here too after death, mahr al-mithl will have no consideration. And according to the two companions, since after the death of the spouses, mahr al-mithl is considered, therefore here too mahr al-mithl will be considered and the woman's heirs will receive mahr al-mithl from the husband's estate.
(And when both spouses die and he had specified a mahr for her, then her heirs may take that from the inheritance of the husband; and if he had not specified a mahr for her, then there is nothing for her heirs according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: for her heirs the mahr in both cases meaning) i.e., the meaning of his statement 'for her heirs the mahr in both cases' is the specified (mahr) in the first case, which is when he specified, and mahr al-mithl in the second case, which is when he did not specify. As for the first case (obligation of the specified), it is because the specified (mahr) is a debt in his liability, either by its proof via evidence or by mutual acknowledgment, and it becomes confirmed by death, so it is paid from his estate – when it is known that both died together, or it is not known which died first, or it is known that the husband died first. But when it is known that she died first, then her share of that (debt) drops. As for the second case, the reasoning of the two (Sahibayn) is that mahr al-mithl becomes a debt in his liability like the specified (mahr), so it does not drop by death, just as when one of them dies. And this is the qiyas of his (Abu Hanifa's) statement, but he (Abu Hanifa) used istihsan (to reject it).
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of mahr al-mithl (proper dower) after the death of both spouses. The usool states: 'لا حكم لمهر المثل عنده بعد موتهما' meaning according to Imam Abu Hanifa, after both spouses die, mahr al-mithl has no legal effect (i.e., the wife's heirs cannot claim it). The two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, holding that mahr al-mithl remains a debt in the husband's estate even after both die.

The Urdu commentary explains the practical application: If both spouses die and the husband had specified a mahr (mahr musamma), the wife's heirs can claim that specified amount from the husband's estate, as it is a confirmed debt. If no mahr was specified, according to Abu Hanifa, the heirs get nothing because after death, mahr al-mithl is not established. According to the Sahibayn, they get mahr al-mithl.

The Arabic text from Al-Inayah provides the detailed ruling and reasoning. It clarifies that the specified mahr is a debt (dayn) in the husband's liability, confirmed by death, so it must be paid from his estate. The ruling applies when both die simultaneously, or when the husband dies first, or when the order of death is unknown. However, if the wife dies first, her share of the mahr debt drops (since the debt was owed to her, it extinguishes with her death, and her heirs do not inherit a debt that was not yet due? Actually the text says 'يسقط نصيبه من ذلك' meaning her share of that (debt) drops if she dies first).

Regarding the second scenario (no specification), the Sahibayn analogize (qiyas) mahr al-mithl to specified mahr: once the marriage is consummated, mahr al-mithl becomes a debt in the husband's liability just like specified mahr, so it should not drop by death. However, Imam Abu Hanifa refutes this by istihsan (juristic preference): he considers that mahr al-mithl is not a debt that can be inherited after both die because its establishment depends on the continuation of the marriage, and after death of both, the marriage is terminated. The text says 'وهو قياس قوله لكن استحسن' meaning this (the Sahibayn's view) is the qiyas of his (Abu Hanifa's) own statement (if he were to apply qiyas), but he (Abu Hanifa) uses istihsan to override it.

This shows the role of istihsan in Hanafi fiqh: Abu Hanifa departs from analogical reasoning based on a stronger legal consideration.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an established case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: setting aside qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence or special consideration.
دين (dayn): A debt or financial obligation in the liability of a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on mahr al-mithl after both spouses die?
A) It is wajib
B) It is not considered
C) It is sunnah
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa denies mahr al-mithl after both die, but the Sahibayn's view (mahr is payable) is the mufta bihi.

Mahr When Both Spouses Die: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Ruling on mahr rights for wife's heirs when both spouses die — an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on mahr when both spouses die and explain the istihsan vs. qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
When both spouses die without a named mahr, Abu Hanifa gives nothing; the Sahibayn require mahr al-mithl — istihsan vs. qiyas.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the payment of mahr (dower) when both spouses die without a named mahr. The key question: does the husband's estate owe mahr al-mithl to the wife's heirs? Abu Hanifa says no, relying on istihsan; his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn), say yes, by qiyas to cases where one spouse dies. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how Hanafi jurists balance textual analogy with juristic preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Recognize the precise scenario: both spouses die without a named mahr, and whether mahr al-mithl is due to the wife's heirs from the husband's estate.
The dispute only arises when no mahr was specified. If a mahr was named, it is unanimously due.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
According to Abu Hanifa, the wife's heirs receive nothing. His basis: after both die, there is no survivor to enforce the obligation, and mahr al-mithl is not established without consummation or specification.
This is an istihsan (juristic preference) deviating from analogy.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
The Sahibayn hold that mahr al-mithl becomes a debt in the husband's liability, analogous to a named mahr, and does not drop by death.
They rely on qiyas: just as mahr al-mithl is due when one spouse dies, it should also be due when both die.
4
Examine the Reasoning
For the named mahr, it is a debt (dayn) confirmed by death; the same logic applies to mahr al-mithl in Sahibayn's view. Abu Hanifa objects that the legal basis for mahr al-mithl (consummation or specification) is absent.
The text says: 'wa huwa qiyasu qawlihi lakin istahsana' – 'that is the analogy of his statement, but he made an exception by istihsan'.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence and Tarjih
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, no payment from the estate; under Sahibayn, the wife's heirs take mahr al-mithl. Later Hanafi practice (mufta bihi) prefers the Sahibayn's view.
Tarjih authority: later scholars like Ibn Abidin favour the Sahibayn, aligning with qiyas and caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت کے لئے مہر مقرر کیا تھا تو اس صورت میں عورت کے ورثاء کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ شوہر کی میراث میں سے اس عورت کا مہر وصول کریں اور اگر عورت کے لئے مہر مقرر نہیں کیا تھا تو اس صورت میں عورت کے ورثاء کے لئے امام صاحب کے نزدیک کچھ بھی نہیں ہو گا جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں مہر مثل ہوگا، کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک زوجین کی وفات کے بعد مہر مثل کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ، لہذا یہاں بھی بعد الوفاۃ مہرمشل کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ بعد وفاة الزوجین مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی مہر مثل کا اعتبار ہوگا اور عورت کے ورثہ شوہر کے ترکہ سے اس عورت کا مہر مثل وصول کریں گے۔
وَإِذَا مَاتَ الزَّوْجَانِ وَقَدْ سَمَّى لَهَا مَهْرًا فَلِوَرَثَتِهَا أَنْ يَأْخُذُوا ذَلِكَ مِنْ مِيرَاثِ الزَّوْجِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ سَمَّى لَهَا مَهْرًا فَلَا شَيْء لِوَرَثَتِهَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ، وَقَالَا: لِوَرَثَتِهَا الْمَهُرُ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ مَعْنَاهُ) أَيْ مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ لِوَرَثَتِهَا الْمَهْرُ فِى الْوَجْهَيْنِ الْمُسَمَّى فِى الْوَجْهِ الْأَوَّلِ وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا سَمَّى (وَمَهُرُ الْمِثْلِ فِى الْوَجْهِ الثَّانِي وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا لَمْ يُسَمٌ (أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ) وَهُوَ وُجُوبُ الْمُسَمَّى (فَلِأَنَّ الْمُسَمَّى دَيْنٌ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ إِمَّا بِقُبُوطِهِ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ أَوْ بِالتَّصَادِقِ وَقَدْ تَأَكَّدَ بِالْمَوْتِ فَيُقْضَى مِنْ تَرِكَتِهِ) إِذَا عُلِمَ أَنَّهُمَا مَاتَا مَعًا أَوْ لَمْ يُعْلَمُ أَيُّهُمَا مَاتَ أَوَّلًا أَوْ عُلِمَ أَنَّ الزَّوْجَ مَاتَ أَوَّلًا، وَأَمَّا إِذَا عُلِمَ أَنَّهَا مَاتَتْ أَوَّلًا فَيَسْقُطُ نَصِيبُهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي فَوَجُهُ قَوْلِهِمَا أَنَّ مَهْرَ الْمِثْلِ صَارَ دَيْنًا فِي ذِمَّتِهِ كَالْمُسَمَّى فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِالْمَوْتِ كَمَا إِذَا مَاتَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَهُوَ قِيَاسُ قَوْلِهِ لَكِنُ اسْتَحْسَنَ .
If the husband had set a mahr for her, then her heirs have the right to take that mahr from the husband's inheritance. And if he had not set a mahr for her, then there is nothing for her heirs according to Abu Hanifa. Both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: there is a mahr for her heirs in both cases. Meaning of his statement: 'there is a mahr for her heirs in both cases' – the named (mahr) in the first case, i.e., when he named (a mahr), and the mahr al-mithl in the second case, i.e., when he did not name. As for the first case – the obligation of the named mahr – because the named mahr is a debt in his liability, either by his acceptance with evidence or by mutual confirmation, and it is confirmed by death, so it is paid from his estate, if it is known that both died together, or it is not known who died first, or it is known that the husband died first. However, if it is known that she died first, then his share of that falls away. As for the second case – the reasoning of their statement (Sahibayn) is that mahr al-mithl becomes a debt in his liability like the named mahr, so it does not drop by death, just as when one of them dies. And that is the analogy of his statement (Abu Hanifa's view), but he made an exception by istihsan.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the payment of mahr when both spouses die without knowing who died first, or both simultaneously. The ruling from Al-Hidayah is presented: if a mahr was named, the wife's heirs take it from the husband's estate. If not named, Abu Hanifa rules no mahr, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule mahr al-mithl. The commentary from Al-Inayah explains the reasoning. For the named mahr, it is a debt (dayn) in the husband's liability, confirmed by death, so it must be paid from his estate. However, if the wife died first, the husband's share of her inheritance from that mahr falls away. For the unnamed mahr, the Sahibayn argue that mahr al-mithl also becomes a debt like the named mahr and does not drop by death, analogizing to the case when one spouse dies. Abu Hanifa's position is based on istihsan, deviating from this analogy, because after both spouses die, there is no surviving party to enforce mahr al-mithl, as the marriage contract is effectively annulled by death without consummation or specification. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn in practice, as the text indicates 'wa huwa qiyasu qawlihi lakin istahsana' – implying Abu Hanifa's istihsan is stated but the Sahibayn's view is the analogy.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife, either specified (musamma) or default (mithl).
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The default dower determined by the bride's status (family, age, beauty, etc.) when no dower is named or the named dower is void.
صاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two chief disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school, when both spouses die without a named mahr, what do the wife's heirs receive?
A) Nothing
B) The named mahr if proven
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) Half of the named mahr

Key Takeaway
When both spouses die without a named mahr, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that the wife's heirs receive mahr al-mithl from the husband's estate, following the Sahibayn's qiyas over Abu Hanifa's istihsan.

Scope of Master's Permission for Slave Marriage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a master's permission for marriage includes invalid contracts, and identify the practical consequence for mahr payment.

Core Idea
A master's permission for marriage is absolute (Abu Hanifa) or only for valid marriage (Sahibayn), affecting whether the slave is sold for mahr immediately.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The question is: when a master gives his slave general permission to marry, does that permission cover only a valid (ja'iz) marriage, or does it also extend to an invalid (fasid) marriage? The answer directly determines how the mahr (dower) is recovered—either by selling the slave immediately or deferring it until the slave's emancipation. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the preferred view in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and the two positions
Read the passage to identify that the dispute is about the scope of 'idhn' (permission) in slave marriage. Abu Hanifa holds it includes both valid and invalid; the Sahibayn restrict it to valid only.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the word 'idhn' is mutlaq (absolute) and should be applied generally. He also notes that some maqasid (purposes) of marriage exist in fasid marriage.
This is a linguistic argument favoring generality.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the primary maqsad of marriage is chastity and protection (i'faf wa tahsin), which is only achieved through a valid marriage. Therefore, permission should be restricted to valid marriage.
This is a teleological (purpose-based) argument.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the slave contracts a fasid marriage with permission: Abu Hanifa rules the slave is sold immediately to pay mahr (as if permitted). The Sahibayn rule the mahr is taken after the slave becomes free (as if unauthorized).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., Ibn Abidin) favour the Sahibayn's view as more precautionary and aligned with the purpose of marriage. Thus, the operative position is that permission only covers valid marriage.
Mufta bihi: slave is not sold; mahr taken after emancipation.

إِنَّ الْإِذْنَ فِي النِّكَاحِ يَنتَظِمُ الْفَاسِدَ وَالْجَائِزَ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ خِلَافًا لَهُمَا. ترجمہ: امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نکاح میں اجازت نکاح فاسد اور جائز دونوں کو شامل ہوتی ہے، صاحبین کا اس میں اختلاف ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک جب آقا اپنے غلام کو نکاح کی اجازت دیدے تو اجازت مطلق ہوتی ہے یہ نکاح صحیح اور فاسد دونوں کو شامل ہوتی ہے، جبکہ صاحبین رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک یہ اجازت صرف نکاح صحیح کی ہوتی ہے نہ کہ نکاح فاسد کی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر آقا نے اپنے غلام سے کہا کہ اس باندی سے نکاح کر لو، پس اس غلام نے اس باندی سے نکاح فاسد کر لیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک مہر میں اس غلام کو بیچا جائے گا جبکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک جب غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا تو اس سے مہر لیا جائے گا۔ امام صاحب کے نزدیک غلام مہر میں اس لئے بیچا جائے گا کہ اس کو آقا نے اجازت دی ہے اور چونکہ یہ اجازت نکاح صحیح کے ساتھ نکاح فاسد کو بھی شامل ہے ، اس لئے کہ لفظ تزوج مطلق ہے جو دونوں کو شامل ہے، جب غلام آقا کی اجازت سے نکاح کرے تو غلام کو مہر میں بیچا جاتا ہے، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی غلام کو بیچا جائے گا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ اجازت صرف نکاح صحیح کی ہوتی ہے تو جب غلام نے نکاح فاسد کیا تو گویا کہ آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر نکاح کیا اور غلام جب آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر نکاح کرلے تو اس صورت میں مہر غلام کی آزادی کے بعد لیا جاتا ہے، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی مہر جب غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا تو اس سے لیا جائے گا۔
الهداية كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق ج ۲ ص ۳۶۰، ط: رحمانيه (قَوْلُهُ: وَالْإِذْنُ فِي النِّكَاحِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْفَاسِدَ أَيْضًا أَى كَمَا يَتَنَاوَلُ الصَّحِيحَ، وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَتَنَاوَلُ إِلَّا الصَّحِيحَ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ النِّكَاحِ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ الْإِعْفَافُ، وَالتَّحْصِينُ وَذَلِكَ بِالْجَائِزِ وَلَهُ أَنَّ اللَّفُظَ مُطْلَقٌ فَيَجْرِى عَلَى إِطْلَاقِهِ، وَبَعْضُ الْمَقَاصِدِ فِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ =
Chapter on marriage of slaves. Indeed, permission in marriage covers the invalid and the valid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (Sahibayn). Translation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, permission in marriage includes both invalid and valid marriage; the Sahibayn differ. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, when a master permits his slave to marry, the permission is absolute and includes both valid and invalid marriage, while according to the Sahibayn, this permission only includes valid marriage, not invalid marriage. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a master told his slave 'marry this slave woman', and the slave entered into an invalid marriage with her, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the slave will be sold to pay the mahr, while according to the Sahibayn, the mahr will be taken from the slave when he becomes free. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the slave is sold for the mahr because the master gave him permission, and since this permission includes both valid and invalid marriage (the word 'tazawwuj' is general covering both), when the marries with permission, the slave is sold for mahr. According to the Sahibayn, since the permission only applies to valid marriage, when the slave made an invalid marriage, it is as if he married without permission, and when a slave marries without permission, the mahr is taken after his emancipation, so here too the mahr will be taken when the slave becomes free. Al-Hidayah: 'His statement: And permission in marriage covers the invalid as well, i.e., just as it covers the valid. This is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Sahibayn) said: It only covers the valid because the purpose of marriage in the future is chastity and protection, and that is achieved by valid (marriage). And for him (Abu Hanifa) that the word is absolute, so it operates according to its absoluteness, and some purposes are found in invalid marriage...' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage discusses the scope of a master's permission for his slave to marry when the slave contracts an invalid (fasid) marriage. The principle is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the permission (idhn) in marriage covers both valid (ja'iz) and invalid (fasid) marriages, while the Sahibayn hold it only covers valid marriages. The practical consequence is how the mahr is paid. If the slave enters an invalid marriage with permission, Abu Hanifa rules that the slave himself is sold to pay the mahr (because the permission includes invalid marriage, so the slave is considered to have acted with permission, and when a slave marries with permission, he is sold for mahr). The Sahibayn rule that the slave is not sold; rather, the mahr is deferred until the slave becomes free, because the permission only covers valid marriage, so an invalid marriage is unauthorized, and for unauthorized marriage, the mahr is taken from the slave after emancipation. The Arabic from Al-Hidayah gives the Sahibayn's proof: the purpose (maqsud) of marriage is chastity (i'faf) and protection (tahsin), which is achieved by valid marriage, so permission should be restricted to valid. Abu Hanifa's proof: the word 'idhn' (permission) is absolute (mutlaq), so it operates generally, and some purposes like procreation (not specified here) are also found in invalid marriage. The passage ends mid-sentence in the Arabic, possibly continuing on the next page.

Key Terms
نکاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage that is defective in a non-essential aspect (e.g., lack of witnesses), which can be rectified or annulled.
نکاح جائز (nikah ja'iz): A valid marriage that fulfills all essential conditions.
اذن (idhn): Permission granted by the master to the slave to enter a marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave contracts an invalid (fasid) marriage with his master's permission, how is the mahr paid according to the mufta bihi (operative view) in the Hanafi school?
A) The slave is sold immediately to pay the mahr.
B) The mahr is taken from the slave after he becomes free.
C) The master pays the mahr himself.
D) The mahr is waived because the marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The scope of a master's permission for slave marriage is restricted to valid contracts in the operative Hanafi position, affecting mahr recovery timing.

Scope of Permission: Valid and Invalid Marriage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of permission for slave marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of a master's permission for his slave's marriage and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A master's permission to marry is absolute and covers both valid and invalid marriage according to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson explores a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school regarding the scope of a master's permission for his slave to contract a marriage. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn), differ on whether such permission extends to invalid (fasid) marriages. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul al-fiqh principles like absolute versus purpose-based interpretation.

Guided Path
1
State the legal problem
Identify the specific question: When a master gives his slave permission to marry, does that permission cover a fasid (invalid) marriage, or only a valid one?
The context is the chapter on marriage of slaves (Bab Nikah al-Raqiq).
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that permission is absolute and includes both valid and invalid. His proof: the word 'idhn is mutlaq (unqualified), so it operates on its generality. Also, some purposes of marriage (like dower obligation) are found in fasid marriage.
The Hidayah states: 'Wa lahu anna al-lafza mutlaq fa yajri ala itlaqihi.'
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad restrict permission to valid marriage only. Their proof: the purpose of marriage is chastity and protection, which are achieved only through a valid marriage.
They argue that the maqsud (objective) guides the interpretation.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If a slave contracts a fasid marriage with permission, Abu Hanifa holds that the slave is sold to pay the dower immediately. The Sahibayn hold that the dower becomes due only after emancipation.
This difference affects the master's liability.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as presented in the Hidayah with his proof highlighted.
Al-Marghinani indicates preference by stating 'lahu' (for him).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب نكاح الرقيق (۳۱) إِنَّ الْإِذْنَ فِي النِّكَاحِ يَنتَظِمُ الْفَاسِدَ وَالْجَائِزَ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ خِلَافًا لَهُمَا.

الهداية كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق ج ۲ ص ۳۶۰، ط: رحمانیه (قَوْلُهُ: وَالْإِذْنُ فِي النِّكَاحِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْفَاسِدَ أَيْضًا أَى كَمَا يَتَنَاوَلُ الصَّحِيحَ، وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَتَنَاوَلُ إِلَّا الصَّحِيحَ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ النِّكَاحِ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ الْإِعْفَافُ، وَالتَّحْصِينُ وَذَلِكَ بِالْجَائِزِ وَلَهُ أَنَّ اللَّفُظَ مُطْلَقٌ فَيَجْرِى عَلَى إِطْلَاقِهِ، وَبَعْضُ الْمَقَاصِدِ فِي النِّكَاحِ الْفَاسِدِ
Chapter on marriage of slaves: (31) Indeed, permission in marriage encompasses the invalid and the permissible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Al-Hidayah: 'His statement: And permission in marriage includes the invalid also, just as it includes the valid. This is according to Abu Hanifa, but they (the two) said: It includes only the valid, because the purpose of marriage in the future is chastity and protection, and that is through the valid (marriage). And for him (Abu Hanifa): The word is absolute, so it operates according to its absoluteness, and some of the purposes are also found in the invalid marriage.'
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding the scope of a master's permission to his slave to marry. The ruling is from Bab Nikah al-Raqiq. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that when a master gives his slave permission to marry, it is absolute and covers both a valid (ja'iz) and an invalid (fasid) marriage. The Sahibayn restrict permission to valid marriage only, arguing that the objective of marriage is chastity (i'faf) and protection (tahsin), which are achieved by a valid marriage, not an invalid one. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the word 'idhn (permission) is unqualified (mutlaq), so it retains its general applicability; moreover, an invalid marriage also fulfills some of these purposes (e.g., proof of lineage, obligation of dower, and waiting period). The practical consequence of this difference appears in the case of a slave who contracts an invalid marriage with the master's permission. According to Abu Hanifa, the slave is sold to pay the dower (a practice in that context), while according to the Sahibayn, the dower becomes due only after the slave is emancipated. The Hidayah text summarizes the arguments: the Sahibayn rely on the purpose (maqsud) of marriage, while Abu Hanifa relies on the absolute nature of the permission.

Key Terms
إذن في النكاح (idhn fi al-nikah): Permission given by a master to his slave to contract a marriage.
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage that is not inherently prohibited but lacks a condition (e.g., no witnesses).
خلافًا لهما (khilafan lahuma): Contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a master gives permission to his slave to marry, does the permission include a fasid (invalid) marriage?
A) No, only valid marriage is included.
B) Yes, it includes both valid and invalid marriage.
C) It depends on the type of fasid marriage.
D) Only if the master explicitly allows it.

Key Takeaway
In intra-Hanafi disputes, the mufta bihi is often the view of Imam Abu Hanifa when his proof relies on the absolute nature of the text.

Maintenance Corresponds to Retention
Ruling on basis of nafaqah being in exchange for detention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that maintenance (nafaqah) is obligatory on the one who retains (ihtabas) and apply it to determine liability in the case of a married slave-girl.

Core Idea
Maintenance is wajib on the retainer, not merely the husband.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of maintenance is not automatically tied to the marriage contract. Rather, it is linked to who actually retains the wife. This principle becomes especially clear in the context of a married slave-girl: if the master keeps her for his service, he must maintain her; if he allots her to her husband, the husband becomes responsible. This lesson examines the proof and application of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The passage states 'al-nafaqah tuqabil al-ihtibas' – maintenance is in exchange for retention. This is the foundational legal maxim governing nafaqah obligations.
The principle is stated as a general rule, not derived from a specific verse or hadith in this text, but it is established through qiyas and the school's methodology.
2
Understand the Scenario
The case is a married slave-girl. The master initially retains her for service, thus he is liable for her maintenance. When he allots her a separate dwelling with her husband (tabwiah), he ceases to retain her, and the husband becomes the retainer.
Retention (ihtibas) can be by either the master or the husband; the maintenance obligation follows the retainer.
3
Apply the Principle to the Ruling
If the master allots a dwelling, the wife has maintenance and dwelling from the husband because the husband now retains her. The text's proof: 'because maintenance corresponds to retention.'
The key is the transfer of retention; the master loses his right to her services? Not entirely, as the next step shows.
4
Note the Master's Retained Right
Even after allotment, the master may reclaim the slave-girl for service. His right to service is not lost by allotment or marriage.
This means the master can at any time reassert retention, and then maintenance would revert to him.
5
Recognize Cross-Madhhab Difference
The Hanafi school ties nafaqah to retention, while other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) tie it solely to the marriage contract. Hence in a case where the husband does not retain the wife (e.g., she is imprisoned), Hanafis would not oblige the husband to pay maintenance.
This difference has practical consequences in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲) إِنَّ النَّفَقَةَ تُقَابِلُ الْإِحْتِبَاسَ . الهداية: كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۳۶۱، ط: رحمانيه

فَإِنْ بَوَّأَهَا مَعَهُ مَنْزِلًا فَلَهَا النَّفَقَةُ وَالسُّكْنَى؛ لأنَّ النَّفَقَةَ تُقَابِلُ الاحْتِبَاسَ، وَلَوْ بَدَا لَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَخْدِمَهَا بَعْدَ التَّبُوئَةِ فَلَهُ ذَلِكَ ؛ لأنَّ حَقَّهُ لَا يَسْقُطُ بِهَا كَمَا لَا يَسْقُطُ بِالنِّكاح. تبيين الحقائق كاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۱۶۴، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية الهداية كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۳۶۱، ط: رحمانی
(32) Indeed, maintenance corresponds to retention. Al-Hidayah: Book of Marriage, Chapter on Marriage of Slaves, vol. 2, p. 361, Rahmania edition. 'Then if he allots a house to her with him, then she has maintenance and dwelling, because maintenance corresponds to retention. And if it occurs to him to use her for service after allotment, he has the right, because his right is not lost by it, just as it is not lost by marriage.' Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Book of Marriage, Chapter on Marriage of Slaves, vol. 2, p. 164, al-Matba'ah al-Kubra al-Amiriyyah. Al-Hidayah, Book of Marriage, Chapter on Marriage of Slaves, vol. 2, p. 361, Rahmania edition.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage establishes a key legal principle: maintenance (nafaqah) is in exchange for retention (ihtibas). The ruling is from the chapter on marriage of slaves. The principle means that the obligation of maintenance does not arise solely from the marriage contract; rather, it is tied to who actually retains the wife. In the context of a slave-girl who is married, if her master retains her for his own service, he is responsible for her maintenance. However, if the master allots (bawwa'a) her a separate dwelling with her husband and does not exercise his right of service, then the husband becomes responsible for her maintenance and lodging. The text further explains that the master does not lose his right to use her for service even after allotment; he may reclaim that right at any time, as his right is not forfeited by the allotment or by the marriage itself. The evidence for this is drawn from the Hidayah and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, both citing the same principle.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter.
احتباس (ihtibas): Retention or detention of the wife by either the husband or the master.
تبوئه (tabwiah): The act of the master allotting a separate dwelling for the slave-girl with her husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'al-nafaqah tuqabil al-ihtibas', who is responsible for the maintenance of a married slave-girl if the master allots her a separate dwelling with her husband?
A) The master, because he still owns her.
B) The husband, because the master has relinquished retention.
C) The state, because it is a public duty.
D) No one, because marriage nullifies maintenance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of maintenance follows retention (ihtibas), not merely the marriage contract.

Nafaqah Corresponds to Restraint: The Legal Maxim and Its Application
Explains the legal maxim that maintenance is compensation for confinement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim 'Nafaqah corresponds to restraint' and apply it to determine liability for maintenance in cases of restraint.

Core Idea
Maintenance is compensation for confinement, not mere marriage.

In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of a husband to provide maintenance to his wife is not automatically triggered by the marriage contract alone. Instead, it is tied to the wife being confined (ihtibas) in the husband's home. This lesson unpacks the maxim 'Nafaqah corresponds to restraint' and its practical application, particularly in the context of a married slave woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its core claim
Read the maxim 'إِنَّ النَّفَقَةَ تُقَابِلُ الْإِحْتِبَاسَ' and understand that nafaqah (maintenance) is a counterpart to ihtibas (restraint).
2
Understand the underlying cause (illah)
The effective cause for nafaqah is the restraint (ihtibas) of the woman, not the marriage contract itself. This is a key Hanafi principle.
Contrast with other schools that see contract as primary.
3
Apply to the case of a married slave woman
Consider two scenarios: (a) master retains her for service – he restrains her, so he is liable; (b) master allocates her to husband's home – husband's restraint, so husband is liable.
The principle determines who bears the expense.
4
Derive the ruling for each scenario
State the hukm: nafaqah is wajib upon the one who exercises ihtibas. Note that the husband's liability for nafaqah for a free wife is also based on ihtibas, though usually presumed.
This maxim also applies to free women, but the slave case makes the cause explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲) إِنَّ النَّفَقَةَ تُقَابِلُ الْإِحْتِبَاسَ .
الهداية: كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۳۶۱، ط: رحمانيه
ترجمہ: خرچہ روکے رکھنے کے مقابلے میں ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر بیوی کا جو نان نفقہ واجب ہوتا ہے یہ اس بیوی کو گھر میں رو کے رکھنے کے عوض اور مقابلے میں ہوتا ہے ، صرف عقد نکاح سے نفقہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر آقا اپنی باندی کا کسی شخص سے نکاح کر دے اور باندی کو اپنی خدمت کے لئے روکے رکھے تو اس وقت باندی کا نان نفقہ اور سکنی کا انتظام آقا پر ہوگا لیکن اگر آقا باندی کو شوہر کے ساتھ ایک مکان میں الگ کر دے اور اپنا حق استخدام چھوڑ دے تو اس وقت باندی کا نان نفقہ اور سکنی وغیرہ شوہر پر لازم ہو گا، اس لئے کہ نفقہ احتباس کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے، پس جس کی طرف سے احتباس پایا جائے گا نفقہ اسی پر لازم ہو گا چاہے آقا ہو یا شوہر ۔
البحر الرائق: كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۳ ص ۲۰۸ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي فَإِنْ بَوَّأَهَا مَعَهُ مَنْزِلًا فَلَهَا النَّفَقَةُ وَالسُّكْنَى؛ لأنَّ النَّفَقَةَ تُقَابِلُ الاحْتِبَاسَ، وَلَوْ بَدَا لَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَخْدِمَهَا بَعْدَ التَّبُوئَةِ فَلَهُ ذَلِكَ ؛ لأنَّ حَقَّهُ لَا يَسْقُطُ بِهَا كَمَا لَا يَسْقُطُ بِالنِّكَاح. تبيين الحقائق كاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۱۶۴، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية الهداية كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۳۶۱، ط: رحمانی
(32) Verily, maintenance corresponds to restraint. Al-Hidayah: Book of Marriage, Chapter on Marriage of Slaves, vol. 2 p. 361, Rahmani edition. Translation: Maintenance is in exchange for keeping (the wife). Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the maintenance which is obligatory upon the husband for his wife is in exchange for keeping her in the house; maintenance is not obligatory by the marriage contract alone. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a master marries his slave woman to someone and keeps her for his own service, the maintenance and housing are upon the master. But if the master allocates her a separate home with the husband and leaves his right of service, then maintenance and housing are upon the husband, because maintenance is due to restraint. So whoever restrains her is liable for maintenance, whether master or husband. Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Book of Marriage, Chapter on Marriage of Slaves, vol. 3 p. 208, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami edition: 'If he allocates her a home with him, then she has maintenance and housing because maintenance corresponds to restraint. And if he later decides to use her for service after allocation, he may do so because his right is not forfeited by that, just as it is not forfeited by marriage.' Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Book of Marriage, Chapter on Marriage of Slaves, vol. 2 p. 164, al-Matba'a al-Kubra al-Amiriyya edition. Al-Hidayah: Book of Marriage, Chapter on Marriage of Slaves, vol. 2 p. 361, Rahmani edition.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage introduces the legal maxim 'Nafaqah corresponds to restraint' (إن النفقة تقابل الاحتباس). The commentator explains that a wife's maintenance is not automatically due upon marriage contract; rather, it is compensation for the wife being confined in the husband's home (احتباس). The text then applies this to the case of a slave woman married by her master: if the master retains her for his own service, he is responsible for her maintenance; if he allocates her a separate home with the husband, the husband becomes liable. The passage cites Al-Hidayah and Al-Bahr al-Raiq to support the ruling.

Key Terms
النَّفَقَة (nafaqah): Maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter.
الْإِحْتِبَاس (ihtibas): Confinement or restraint of the wife in the husband's home.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim 'Nafaqah corresponds to restraint', who is liable for the maintenance of a married slave woman if the master retains her for his service?
A) The husband
B) The master
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Maintenance is owed by the person who exercises restraint over the woman, whether husband or master.

Nikah — Marriage

Killing is Treated as Destruction in Worldly Rulings
Establishes the principle that killing is destruction and applies it to mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that killing is considered destruction (itlaf) to determine the liability of mahr when the subject matter of marriage is destroyed before consummation.

Core Idea
Killing in worldly rulings is destruction — intentional destruction of the subject matter forfeits its substitute (mahr).

This lesson establishes a central Hanafi maxim: killing (qatl) is legally classified as destruction (itlaf) in all worldly contexts. While commonly associated with criminal penalties like qisas and diyah, this principle extends to civil obligations, particularly the entitlement to mahr when the subject matter of the marriage (the slave) is destroyed before consummation. The lesson unpacks the maxim and applies it to a specific dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
State the principle that killing is treated as destruction in worldly rulings. Understand that this classification triggers legal consequences like qisas, diyah, and forfeiture of mahr.
The maxim is: 'إن القتل في أحكام الدنيا جعل إتلافًا'.
2
Understand the analogy to mahr
When a master kills his married slave before consummation, he destroys the object of exchange (ownership of the private part). According to the principle, this destruction of the subject matter voids its substitute (mahr).
Analogous to a seller destroying the sold item before delivery.
3
Trace the dispute with the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds that mahr is forfeited immediately. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that mahr remains due because killing is like natural death, which does not void mahr.
The Sahibayn analogize to natural death; Abu Hanifa distinguishes killing as a deliberate act of destruction.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that killing is not like natural death; it is a deliberate act of destruction. Evidence: qisas and diyah are imposed because killing is destruction. Therefore, the analogy to a seller destroying the sold item is more appropriate.
This aligns with the general principle that killing is treated as itlaf.
5
Apply to the case
In the scenario of a master killing his slave before consummation, Abu Hanifa rules that the master loses the mahr. The Sahibayn rule that the husband is liable and the master's heirs receive it.
The practical difference: immediate forfeiture vs. mahr being paid to the master's estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۳) إِنَّ الْقَتْلَ فِي أَحْكَامِ الدُّنْيَا جُعِلَ إِتَلَافًا.
ترجمه قبل کو دنیاوی احکام میں اتلاف شمار کیا گیا ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کسی کو قتل کرنا اس کو دنیاوی احکامات میں اختلاف شمار کر کے قتل محمد میں قاتل پر قصاص اور قتل خطا میں اس پر دیتے واجب کی جاتی ہے۔ جس طرح قتل قصاص وغیرہ کے سلسلے میں اتلاف ہے اسی طرح مہر کے متعلق بھی وہ اتلاف ہوگا اور مہر کا اتلاف = حَاصِلٌ كَالنَّسَبِ وَوُجُوبِ الْمَهُرِ، وَالْعِدَّةِ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ وُجُودِ الْوَطْءِ وَفَائِدَةُ الْخِلَافِ تَظْهَرُ فِي حَقِّ لُزُومِ الْمَهُرِ فِيمَا إِذَا تَزَوَّجَ امْرَأَةً نِكَاحًا فَاسِدًا وَدَخَلَ بِهَا لِأَنَّهُ يُبَاعُ فِي الْمَهْرِ عِنْدَهُ وَعِندَهُمَا لَا يُطَالَبُ إلَّا بَعدَ العِشق.
البحر الرائق: كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۳ ص ۲۰۸ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي فَإِنْ بَوَّأَهَا مَعَهُ مَنْزِلًا فَلَهَا النَّفَقَةُ وَالسُّكْنَى؛ لأنَّ النَّفَقَةَ تُقَابِلُ الاحْتِبَاسَ، وَلَوْ بَدَا لَهُ أَنْ يَسْتَخْدِمَهَا بَعْدَ التَّبُوئَةِ فَلَهُ ذَلِكَ ؛ لأنَّ حَقَّهُ لَا يَسْقُطُ بِهَا كَمَا لَا يَسْقُطُ بِالنِّكَاح. تبيين الحقائق كاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۱۶۴، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية الهداية كتاب النكاح، باب نكاح الرقيق، ج ۲ ص ۳۶۱، ط: رحمانی
اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی یہی ہے کہ قاتل کو کچھ بھی مہر نہ ملے اور جو کچھ نکاح سے ثابت اور واجب ہوا تھاوہ ساقط ہو جائے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر آقا نے اپنی باندی کی کسی سے شادی کرادی پھر اس باندی کے ساتھ ابھی تک اس کے شوہر نے دخول نہیں کیا تھا کہ آقا نے اس باندی کو قتل کر ڈالا تو اب امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس قاتل آقا کے لئے اس باندی کا مہر نہیں ہوگا یعنی یہ اس کے مہر سے محروم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ قتل احکام دنیا میں تلف کرنا ہے اور جب آقا نے قبل الدخول اس باندی کو قتل کر دیا تو گویا کہ اس نے معوض عنہ یعنی ملک بضع کو شوہر کے سپر د کرنے سے پہلے ہلاک کر دیا ، جب مبدل اور معوض یعنی ملک بضع ہلاک ہو گیا تو اُس کا بدل یعنی مہر بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا اور آقا مہر سے محروم ہو گا، جس طرح مسلمان عورت نکاح کے بعد خلوت اور صحبت سے پہلے مرتد ہو جائے تو منع مبدل کی وجہ سے اُسے بھی بدل یعنی مہر سے محروم کیا جائے گا، اسی طرح یہاں بھی آقا مہر سے محروم ہو گا، جبکہ صاحبین یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح طبعی موت مرنے سے مہر ساقط نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح قتل سے بھی مہر ساقط نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے وقت مقرر پر مری ہے، اس لئے شوہر پر مہر لازم ہوگا اور وہ مہر آقا کو ملے گا ، صاحبین کے قیاس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قتل کو دنیاوی احکامات میں اتلاف شمار کیا گیا ہے، جس طرح قتلِ عمد میں قاتل پر قصاص اور قتل خطاء میں دیست لازم ہوتی ہے، اسی طرح مہر کے سلسلے میں بھی یہ اختلاف شمار ہوگا اور قاتل کو کچھ مہر نہ ملے گا۔
(33) Verily, killing in worldly rulings is made destruction. Translation: Killing is considered destruction in worldly rulings. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that killing someone is considered as destruction in worldly rulings, so that in intentional murder, qisas is obligatory on the killer, and in accidental killing, diyah is obligatory. Just as killing is destruction in matters of qisas etc., similarly it is destruction concerning mahr. And the destruction of mahr results in (the ruling) being like that of lineage and obligation of mahr and waiting period according to the existence of intercourse. And the benefit of the dispute appears regarding the liability of mahr in the case where a man marries a woman in a fasid marriage and consummates, because according to him (Abu Hanifa) the mahr is due immediately, while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is not demanded except after separation. Al-Bahr al-Raiq: ... [same quote as in lesson 1] ... The principle is that the killer gets no mahr, and what was established by the marriage becomes void. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a master marries his slave woman to someone, then before the husband consummates, the master kills her, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the killer master gets no mahr from the slave, i.e., he is deprived of her mahr. Because killing in worldly matters is destruction, and when the master killed her before consummation, it is as if he destroyed the object of exchange (ownership of the private part) before delivering it to the husband. When the original subject matter (ownership of the private part) is destroyed, its substitute (mahr) also falls, and the master is deprived. Similar to the case of a free woman who apostatizes after marriage but before seclusion and intercourse: she is deprived of mahr due to prevention of the subject matter. Similarly here the master is deprived. Whereas the Sahibayn say: Just as natural death does not nullify mahr, similarly killing does not nullify it because she died at her appointed time. Therefore, the husband is liable for mahr and the master gets it. The response to the Sahibayn's analogy is that killing is considered destruction in worldly rulings, as in intentional murder qisas is obligatory and in accidental killing diyah is obligatory, so similarly in the case of mahr, it is considered destruction and the killer gets no mahr.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents the second maxim: 'Killing in worldly rulings is treated as destruction' (إن القتل في أحكام الدنيا جعل إتلافًا). The commentator explains that murder is considered an act of destruction in Islamic law, which triggers consequences such as qisas (retaliation) for intentional killing and diyah (blood money) for manslaughter. Similarly, in the context of mahr (dower), if a master kills his slave he married off before consummation, the mahr is considered destroyed and the master cannot claim it. The text also discusses a benefit of a dispute concerning mahr in a fasid marriage: according to Abu Hanifa, the mahr is due immediately upon consummation; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is only due after separation (like in an invalid marriage). The passage then details the application to the master killing his slave: Abu Hanifa rules that the master loses the mahr because he destroyed the subject matter (mabdhal) before delivery, analogizing to a free woman who apostatizes before consummation or a seller who destroys the sold item before delivery. The Sahibayn analogize to natural death, but the Hanafi response distinguishes killing as a deliberate destruction, citing qisas and diyah as evidence.

Key Terms
الْقَتْل (qatl): Killing; considered as destruction (itlaf) in worldly rulings.
إِتَلَاف (itlaf): Destruction of property or legal subject matter.
بَدَل (badal): Substitute; the counter-value in an exchange, such as mahr as substitute for ownership of the private part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The master is still entitled to mahr
B) The husband must still pay the mahr to the master's heirs
C) The master loses the right to mahr
D) The mahr is divided between the master and the husband

Key Takeaway
Killing in worldly rulings is legally destruction — intentional destruction of the subject matter before delivery forfeits its substitute (mahr).
