Marriage is for Benefits – Application to Apostate Women
Explaining that marriage is legislated for its benefits, applied to the case of an apostate woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that marriage is legislated for its benefits and apply it to derive the ruling that an apostate woman cannot marry anyone.

Core Idea
Marriage is legislated for its benefits, not as an end in itself.

This lesson explores a foundational principle of Hanafi marriage law: marriage is not an act purely for its own sake but a means to achieve specific benefits (masalih) such as dwelling, companionship, and procreation. The great Hanafi jurist al-Marghinani applies this principle to the situation of an apostate woman, showing how the prohibition of her marriage follows directly from the very purpose of the institution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the opening statement: 'marriage was not legislated for its own sake but for its benefits.' Understand that this is the core legal maxim guiding the ruling.
This is a talil (causative) argument.
2
Understand the benefits (masalih)
Identify the benefits listed: dwelling (sukni), companionship (izdiwaj), procreation (tawalud wa tanasul). These are the purposes the Shari'ah aims to achieve through marriage.
3
Apply the principle to the apostate woman
Consider the two reasons given: (1) she is confined for reflection and marriage would distract her, and (2) the benefits of marriage cannot be realized between spouses who do not share the same faith.
The benefits require mutual harmony and cooperation, which are absent with an apostate.
4
Derive the ruling
Since marriage fails to achieve its intended benefits and actively hinders repentance, it is prohibited (haram) and invalid (batil) for an apostate woman to contract marriage with anyone.
The text uses 'one' in a negative context to indicate universal prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن النكاح ما شرع لعينه بل لمصالحه. ترجمہ: نکاح اپنے عین کے لئے مشروع نہیں کیا گیا ہے بلکہ وہ تو اپنے مصالح کی غرض سے مشروع کیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شریعت نے نکاح صرف خواہشات نفسانی کو پورا کرنے کے لئے مشروع نہیں کیا بلکہ نکاح مصالح نکاح کے لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے، نکاح کے مصالح سکنی ، ازدواج ، توالد و تناسل وغیرہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ مرتد پعورت نہ کسی مسلمان مرد سے نکاح کر سکتی ہے اور نہ کسی کافر سے، کیونکہ ان کے ساتھ نکاح مصالح نکاح کو شامل نہیں ہے یعنی ان کے مابین جو نکاح کے مصالح ہیں وہ حاصل نہیں ہو سکتے اور چونکہ نکاح ذات نکاح کی حیثیت سے مشروع نہیں ہے بلکہ مصالح نکاح کے لئے مشروع ہے، مرتد ہ کو محبوس کیا جائے گا تا کہ وہ غور وفکر کر کے اپنے شبہات دور کرے، اور شوہر کی خدمت اس کو غور وفکر کرنے سے غافل کر دے گی ،اس لئے اس کے حق میں نکاح مشروع نہیں ہے، نیز مصالح نکاح زوجین کے درمیان حاصل نہیں ہوسکتا، نکاح لذاتہ مشروع نہیں ہے، بلکہ نکاح مصالح کے لئے مشروع ہے، اور نکاح کے مصالح سکنی توالد و تناسل وغیرہ ہے۔ وَأَمَّا الْمُرْتَدَّةُ فَلَانَّهَا مَحْبُوسَةٌ لِلتَّأمل وَخِدْمَهُ الزَّوْجِ تَشْغَلُهَا عَنْهُ وَلَأَنَّهُ لَا يَنْتَظِمُ بَيْنَهُمَا الْمَصَالِحُ، وَالنِّكَاحُ مَا شُرِعَ لِعَيْنِهِ بَلْ لِمَصَالِحِهِ وَعَبَّرَ بِأَحَدٍ فِي سِيَاقِ النَّفْيِ لِيُفِيدَ الْعُمُومَ فَلا يَتَزَوَّجُ الْمُرْتَدُّ مُسْلِمَةً وَلَا كِتَابِيَّةً وَلَا مُرْتَدَّةً وَلَا يَتَزَوَّجُ الْمُرْتَدَّةَ مُسْلِمٌ وَلَا كَافِرٌ وَلَا مُرْتَدُّ .
Indeed, marriage was not legislated for its own sake but for its benefits. Translation: Marriage was not legislated for its own essence; rather, it was legislated for its benefits. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the Shariah did not legislate marriage merely to fulfill carnal desires, but marriage was legislated for the benefits of marriage. The benefits of marriage are dwelling, companionship, procreation, etc. The author of Al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that an apostate woman cannot marry any Muslim man nor any disbeliever, because with them marriage does not encompass the benefits of marriage, meaning the benefits of marriage cannot be achieved between them. And since marriage was not legislated as an end in itself but for its benefits, and an apostate woman is confined for reflection, and serving her husband would distract her from that, therefore marriage is not legislated for her. Also, the benefits of marriage cannot be achieved between the spouses; marriage is not legislated for its own sake but for its benefits. And as for the apostate woman, she is confined for reflection, and serving her husband would distract her from it, and because the benefits cannot be realized between them, and marriage was not legislated for its own sake but for its benefits. And he expressed 'one' in the context of negation to denote generality, so an apostate man cannot marry a Muslim woman, a kitabiyya, or an apostate woman, and an apostate woman cannot be married by a Muslim, a disbeliever, or an apostate.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This lesson presents the principle that marriage is not an end in itself but a means to achieve certain benefits (masalih) such as dwelling, companionship, and procreation. The author applies this principle to the ruling concerning apostate women (murtaddah). Since an apostate woman is imprisoned to reflect on her doubts and recant, marriage would distract her from this purpose. Moreover, the benefits of marriage cannot be properly realized between spouses if one is an apostate because the marital relationship requires mutual harmony in faith. Therefore, an apostate woman cannot marry anyone—whether Muslim, Kitabi, or another apostate. Similarly, an apostate man is also prohibited from marrying Muslim women, Kitabiyyat, or apostate women. The text uses the word 'one' in a negative context to indicate complete universality.

Key Terms
مصالح (masalih): Benefits or purposes of marriage, such as dwelling, companionship, procreation.
سكنى (sukni): Dwelling; the marital home and the comfort derived from living together.
ازدواج (izdiwaj): Companionship and union between spouses.
توالد وتناسل (tawalud wa tanasul): Procreation and multiplication of offspring.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't an apostate woman marry anyone according to this lesson?
A) Because she is considered legally dead.
B) Because marriage benefits cannot be achieved and it distracts her from repentance.
C) Because she can only marry another apostate.
D) Because her previous marriage is still valid.

Key Takeaway
Marriage's prohibition for apostates stems from the principle that marriage is a means to achieve specific benefits, not an end in itself.

Why Apostates Cannot Marry: Prohibition and Rational Proof
Explaining the prohibition of marriage for apostates using rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage of apostates and explain the rationale based on the purposes of marriage (masalih al-nikah) and the requirement of imprisonment for reflection.

Core Idea
An apostate's marriage is invalid because it conflicts with the purpose of marriage and the requirement of imprisonment for reflection.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explains why an apostate (murtadd) cannot contract a valid marriage. The ruling is rooted in the principle that marriage is legislated not for its own sake, but for its benefits (masalih), such as dwelling, intimacy, and procreation. An apostate is required to be imprisoned to reflect on their doubts and return to Islam, and marriage would distract them from this critical reflection. Moreover, the necessary harmony for achieving marital benefits is absent between an apostate and a believer or even another apostate. The text emphasizes the universality of the prohibition: an apostate cannot marry anyone, and no one can marry an apostate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage rules that an apostate (male or female) cannot contract a valid marriage with anyone—Muslim, Kitabiyya, or fellow apostate. The ruling is that such a marriage is invalid (batil).
The ruling covers all possible spouses.
2
Extract the underlying principle
The author states that marriage is legislated for its benefits (masalih), not for its own sake. This principle is the foundation for the prohibition.
The benefits include dwelling, intimacy, procreation, etc.
3
Understand the special condition of the apostate
An apostate is required to be imprisoned for reflection (tadbīr) to remove doubts and repent. Marriage would distract them from this essential act of reflection.
The service of a spouse would occupy the apostate's time and attention.
4
Apply the principle to the case
Since the benefits of marriage cannot be achieved between an apostate and any spouse, and since marriage would hinder the apostate's reflection, the marriage is not legislated and is therefore invalid.
The absence of faith and harmony prevents the attainment of marital benefits.
5
Note the universal scope
The text uses a general negation to cover all possibilities: an apostate cannot marry a Muslim, a Kitabiyya, or another apostate; similarly, an apostate woman cannot be married by a Muslim, a non-Muslim, or another apostate.
No exception is made for any type of spouse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصالح سکنی ، ازدواج ، توالد و تناسل وغیرہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ مرتد پعورت نہ کسی مسلمان مرد سے نکاح کر سکتی ہے اور نہ کسی کافر سے، کیونکہ ان کے ساتھ نکاح مصالح نکاح کو شامل نہیں ہے یعنی ان کے مابین جو نکاح کے مصالح ہیں وہ حاصل نہیں ہو سکتے اور چونکہ نکاح ذات نکاح کی حیثیت سے مشروع نہیں ہے بلکہ مصالح نکاح کے لئے مشروع ہے، مرتد ہ کو محبوس کیا جائے گا تا کہ وہ غور وفکر کر کے اپنے شبہات دور کرے، اور شوہر کی خدمت اس کو غور وفکر کرنے سے غافل کر دے گی ،اس لئے اس کے حق میں نکاح مشروع نہیں ہے، نیز مصالح نکاح زوجین کے درمیان حاصل نہیں ہوسکتا، نکاح لذاتہ مشروع نہیں ہے، بلکہ نکاح مصالح کے لئے مشروع ہے، اور نکاح کے مصالح سکنی توالد و تناسل وغیرہ ہے۔ وَأَمَّا الْمُرْتَدَّةُ فَلَانَّهَا مَحْبُوسَةٌ لِلتَّأمل وَخِدْمَهُ الزَّوْجِ تَشْغَلُهَا عَنْهُ وَلَأَنَّهُ لَا يَنْتَظِمُ بَيْنَهُمَا الْمَصَالِحُ، وَالنِّكَاحُ مَا شُرِعَ لِعَيْنِهِ بَلْ لِمَصَالِحِهِ وَعَبَّرَ بِأَحَدٍ فِي سِيَاقِ النَّفْيِ لِيُفِيدَ الْعُمُومَ فَلا يَتَزَوَّجُ الْمُرْتَدُّ مُسْلِمَةً وَلَا كِتَابِيَّةً وَلَا مُرْتَدَّةً وَلَا يَتَزَوَّجُ الْمُرْتَدَّةَ مُسْلِمٌ وَلَا كَافِرٌ وَلَا مُرْتَدُّ .
The benefits of marriage such as dwelling, intimacy, procreation, etc. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning the aforementioned principle, is explaining that an apostate woman cannot marry a Muslim man nor a non-Muslim, because marriage with them does not include the benefits of marriage, i.e., the benefits of marriage between them cannot be achieved. And since marriage is not legislated for its own sake but for the benefits of marriage, the apostate woman will be imprisoned so that she may reflect and remove her doubts, and the service of the husband would distract her from that. Therefore, marriage is not legislated for her. Also, the benefits of marriage cannot be achieved between the spouses. Marriage is not legislated for its own sake, but for its benefits, and the benefits of marriage are dwelling, procreation, etc. And as for the apostate woman, because she is imprisoned for reflection, and the service of the husband would distract her from it, and because the benefits cannot be arranged between them, and marriage was only legislated for its benefits, not for its own sake. And he expressed with 'one' in the context of negation to indicate generality. So an apostate cannot marry a Muslim woman, nor a Kitabiyyah, nor an apostate woman. And an apostate woman cannot be married by a Muslim, nor a non-Muslim, nor an apostate.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with rational proof. The author explains why an apostate (murtadd) cannot contract a valid marriage. The key reason is that marriage is legislated for the sake of its benefits (masalih), such as dwelling together, intimacy, and procreation. An apostate is required to be imprisoned to reflect on their doubts and hopefully return to Islam. If they were allowed to marry, the service of the spouse would distract them from this essential reflection. Moreover, the benefits of marriage cannot be truly achieved between an apostate and a Muslim or non-Muslim because the necessary harmony and faith are absent. The Arabic quotation from Bahr al-Raiq confirms that an apostate cannot marry anyone: neither a Muslim woman, nor a Kitabiyyah (Jewish/Christian), nor a fellow apostate. Similarly, an apostate woman cannot be married by a Muslim, a non-Muslim, or another apostate. The principle 'marriage is legislated for its benefits' is the underlying cause ('illa) for this prohibition. The text emphasizes generality by using the word 'one' in negation, covering all possible spouses.

Key Terms
مصالح نکاح (masalih al-nikah): The benefits/purposes of marriage, including dwelling, intimacy, procreation, etc.
مرتد (murtadd): A person who has apostatized from Islam.
محبوس (mahbus): Imprisoned or confined, specifically for the apostate to reflect on their doubts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because marriage is only for Muslims.
B) Because the apostate is imprisoned for reflection and marriage would distract them, and the benefits of marriage cannot be achieved.
C) Because apostates cannot have children.
D) Because marriage is not legislated for anyone.

Key Takeaway
Marriage of an apostate is invalid (batil) because it contradicts the purpose of marriage and the requirement of imprisonment for reflection.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Ownership and Marriage Are Mutually Exclusive
Establishes legal principle with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why milk al-yamin and milk al-nikah are contradictory and apply the ruling that ownership between spouses voids the marriage immediately.

Core Idea
Ownership (milk al-yamin) and marriage (milk al-nikah) cannot coexist; the stronger right overrides the weaker.

This lesson explores a fundamental Hanafi principle: the contradiction between ownership and marital rights. When a husband acquires ownership of his wife (e.g., by purchasing her as a slave) or vice versa, the marriage becomes void immediately. The reasoning is rooted in the nature of milk al-nikah as a necessity-based right that cannot stand against the stronger right of ownership. Understanding this principle clarifies many rulings on the intersection of slavery and marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rights
Milk al-yamin (ownership by right hand) is a strong, permanent ownership over a slave or property. Milk al-nikah (marital right) is the husband's authority over his wife, established by necessity (darurah) for procreation.
Milk al-nikah is a departure from the default freedom of a woman.
2
Understand why they conflict
If both existed simultaneously, one person would be both owner and owned, which is impossible. Hence they are mutually exclusive (munafi).
The conflict is logical, not merely regulatory.
3
Apply the principle to specific cases
The passage lists four scenarios: husband owns wife (or part of her), wife owns husband (or part of him). In all four, marriage becomes void.
Partial ownership (shiqs) also suffices.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
Milk al-nikah is established khilaf al-qiyas (contrary to analogy) due to necessity. Necessity is limited (al-darurah tuqaddaru bi qadariha). Milk al-yamin is the stronger right (qawi), so it overrides the necessity-based right.
This is aqli (rational) proof: the weaker yields to the stronger.
5
Conclude the ruling
Once ownership is acquired, marriage is batil (void) immediately. No divorce or additional action is required.
Some later Hanafi authorities discuss if separation is faskh or talaq, but here it is voidness of the original contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۲) إِنَّ مِلْكَ الْيَمِينِ يُنَافِي مِلْكَ النِّكَاحِ.
ترجمہ: ملک یمین ملک نکاح کے منافی ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ملک نکاح اور ملک ببین آپس میں دو متضاد چیزیں ہیں ایک ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوسکتیں ، کیونکہ ملک یمین اگر ملک نکاح کے ساتھ جمع ہو جائے تو شخص واحد کا مالک اور مملوک ہونا لا زم آئے گا جو درست نہیں۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر شوہر بیوی کا مالک بن جائے یا بیوی کے ایک حصے کا یا بیوی اپنے شوہر کی مالکہ بن جائے یا شوہر کے ایک حصے کی ، تو دونوں میں فرقت واقع ہوگی، کیونکہ ملک یمین ملک نکاح کے منافی ہے اور مذکورہ مسئلہ میں دو متضاد ملکیتیوں کا اجتماع ہوا اور دو متضاد ملک کا اجتماع باطل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ملک نکاح کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عورت شوہر کی مملوکہ ہو اور شراء وغیرہ سے حاصل ہونے والی ملک یعنی ملک یمین کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عورت مالکن ہو ، اور یہ دونوں ناممکن ہیں، اس لئے مالکیت اور مملوکیت کے اجتماع کی وجہ سے ان کا نکاح ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح شوہر بیوی کا مالک ہو جائے تو بھی دونوں میں فرقت ہو جائے گی ، اس لئے کہ شوہر کے لئے جو ملک نکاح ثابت ہے وہ بر بنائے ضرورت ہے، اس لئے بیوی آزاد، عاقل، بالغ عورت ہے اور آزاد ہر طرح کی قید و بند سے آزاد ہوتا ہے، مگر پھر بھی ضرورت توالد و تناسل کے تحت خلاف قیاس عورت پر شوہر کی ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ہے، اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ الضرورة تتقدر بقدرها “ یعنی خلاف قیاس ہونے والی چیز ضرور تا ہی ثابت ہوتی ہے،اس لئے شوہر کی ملک نکاح ضروری ہے اور شراء ہبہ وغیرہ کے ذریعے عورت جب اس کی ملکیت میں آجائے گی تو اسے اس پر ملک یمین حاصل ہو گی ، جو ملک قوی ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ ملک قوی کے مقابلے میں ملک ضروری باقی نہیں رہ سکتی ، اس لئے قومی ملک یمین حاصل ہوتے ہی ملک ضروری یعنی ملک نکاح ختم ہو جائے گی ۔
(۲۳) إِنَّ الشَّرُطَ مَا يَكُونُ مَعْدُومًا عَلَى خَطَرِ الْوُجُودِ وَالْحُكْمُ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ.
وَلَوْ مَلَكَهَا أَوْ شِقْصَهَا أَوْ مَلَكَتْهُ أَوْ شِقْصَهُ بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ يَعْنِي لَوْ مَلَكَ الزَّوْجُ امْرَأَتَهُ بِأَنْ كَانَتْ أَمَةً أَوْ مَلَكَ جُزْءا مِنْهَا أَوْ كَانَتْ هِيَ الْمَالِكَةُ لِزَوْجِهَا أَوْ لِجُزْئِهِ بَطَلَ النِّكَاحُ. وَأَمَّا مِلْكُهَا إِيَّاهُ فَلِلاجْتِمَاعِ بَيْنَ الْمَالِكِيَّةِ وَالْمَمْلُوكِيَّةِ فَلَا يَنْتَظِمُ الْمَصَالِحُ وَهُوَ مَا شُرِعَ إِلَّا لِمَصَالِحِهِ، وَأَمَّا مِلْكُهُ إِيَّاهَا فَلانَّ مِلكَ النِّكَاحِ ضَرُورِيٌّ وَقَدْ اسْتَغْنَى عَنْهُ بِالْأَقْوَى لِقُبُوتِ الحل به. تبيين الحقائق كتاب الطلاق فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان، ج ۲ ص ۲۰۹، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية الهداية كاب الطلاق، فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان ، ج ۲ ص ۳۸۵، ط: رحمانیه
(22) Indeed, ownership by right hand (milk al-yamin) conflicts with marital right (milk al-nikah). Translation: Milk al-yamin conflicts with milk al-nikah. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that milk al-nikah and milk al-yamin are two contradictory things and cannot combine, because if milk al-yamin combines with milk al-nikah, then one person would be both owner and owned, which is not valid. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if the husband becomes the owner of his wife, or part of her, or the wife becomes the owner of her husband or part of him, then separation occurs between them, because milk al-yamin conflicts with milk al-nikah, and in the mentioned case, there is a combination of two contradictory ownerships, and the combination of two contradictory ownerships is void. This is because milk al-nikah requires the woman to be owned by the husband, while milk al-yamin acquired through purchase etc. requires the woman to be the owner, and these are impossible. Thus, due to the combination of ownership and being owned, their marriage will terminate. Similarly, if the husband becomes the owner of the wife, separation will also occur because the milk al-nikah established for the husband is based on necessity. The wife is a free, sane, adult woman, and a free person is free from all kinds of restrictions. Yet, due to the necessity of reproduction, contrary to analogy, the husband's ownership over the wife is established. The rule is that necessity is limited to its extent. Therefore, the husband's milk al-nikah is necessary, and when the woman comes into his ownership through purchase or gift, he obtains milk al-yamin over her, which is strong ownership. It is clear that the necessary ownership cannot remain in the face of strong ownership, so once strong milk al-yamin is obtained, the necessary milk al-nikah terminates. (23) Indeed, a condition is something that is non-existent with the possibility of existence, and the ruling is attached to it. And if he owns her or part of her, or she owns him or part of him, the contract becomes void, meaning if the husband owns his wife by her being a slave, or owns part of her, or she is the owner of her husband or part of him, the marriage becomes void. As for her owning him, it is due to the combination of ownership and being owned, so interests cannot be organized, and marriage was legislated only for its interests. As for him owning her, it is because the marital right is one of necessity, and it is dispensed with by the stronger (right) through the acceptance of dissolution (by it).
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents two legal principles from al-Hidayah. The first principle (22) states that milk al-yamin (ownership by purchase etc.) conflicts with milk al-nikah (marital right). The author explains that these two rights cannot coexist because they would necessitate one person being both owner and owned simultaneously, which is invalid. The passage then applies this principle: if the husband acquires ownership of his wife (e.g., she is a slave and he buys her), or a part of her, or vice versa, the marriage becomes void (batil). The reasoning is that milk al-nikah is based on necessity (darurah) for procreation, while milk al-yamin is a strong ownership right. When the stronger right (milk al-yamin) appears, the necessary right (milk al-nikah) is overridden because a necessary right remains only as long as there is no stronger right. The second principle (23) defines a condition (shart) as something non-existent with the possibility of existence. The subsequent Arabic quote from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq reiterates the ruling about ownership conflict, confirming the voidness of marriage in such cases.

Key Terms
ملك اليمين (milk al-yamin): Ownership by right of possession, acquired through purchase, gift, or inheritance, typically over a slave or property.
ملك النكاح (milk al-nikah): The right of marriage, i.e., the husband's right over his wife based on necessity (darurah) for procreation.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity; the basis for milk al-nikah, which is established as a departure from analogy (khilaf al-qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'Inna milk al-yamin yunafi milk al-nikah', what happens if a husband purchases his wife as a slave?
A) The marriage continues as before because marriage is stronger than ownership.
B) The marriage becomes void (batil) and separation occurs immediately.
C) The wife becomes free and the marriage is annulled.
D) The husband must divorce her for the ownership to take effect.

Key Takeaway
Milk al-yamin and milk al-nikah cannot coexist; acquisition of ownership over a spouse voids the marriage immediately.

Nullification of Marriage Due to Ownership Between Spouses
Explaining the ruling when a spouse becomes owner of the other

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on nullification of marriage when a spouse becomes the owner of the other, and apply the legal maxim of necessity to distinguish between milk al-nikah and milk al-yamin.

Core Idea
When ownership (milk al-yamin) overtakes marriage ownership (milk al-nikah), the marriage is nullified.

This passage from Al-Hidayah and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq explains a unique Hanafi ruling: if a spouse acquires full or partial ownership over the other, the marriage contract becomes void. The reasoning hinges on the distinction between two types of ownership—necessity-based marriage rights and absolute property rights. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping Hanafi nikah jurisprudence and the application of the maxim 'necessity is measured by its extent.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: (1) wife owns husband (or part), (2) husband owns wife (or part). Both lead to nullification.
Partial ownership (shiqs) is explicitly included.
2
Distinguish the two types of ownership
Marriage ownership (milk al-nikah) is necessity-based and weak; property ownership (milk al-yamin) is absolute and strong.
This distinction is key to the Hanafi reasoning.
3
Apply the maxim 'al-darurah tuqaddaru biqadariha'
The necessity-based ownership is limited; when stronger ownership arises, the necessity ends.
The maxim limits the scope of the exception to marriage.
4
Trace the qiyas reasoning
In the wife-owns-husband case, the contradiction of being both owner and owned nullifies marriage; in the husband-owns-wife case, the stronger ownership overrides the weaker.
Both rely on the incompatibility of concurrent ownerships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بیوی کے ایک حصے کا یا بیوی اپنے شوہر کی مالکہ بن جائے یا شوہر کے ایک حصے کی ، تو دونوں میں فرقت واقع ہوگی، کیونکہ ملک یمین ملک نکاح کے منافی ہے اور مذکورہ مسئلہ میں دو متضاد ملکیتیوں کا اجتماع ہوا اور دو متضاد ملک کا اجتماع باطل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ملک نکاح کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عورت شوہر کی مملوکہ ہو اور شراء وغیرہ سے حاصل ہونے والی ملک یعنی ملک یمین کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عورت مالکن ہو ، اور یہ دونوں ناممکن ہیں، اس لئے مالکیت اور مملوکیت کے اجتماع کی وجہ سے ان کا نکاح ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح شوہر بیوی کا مالک ہو جائے تو بھی دونوں میں فرقت ہو جائے گی ، اس لئے کہ شوہر کے لئے جو ملک نکاح ثابت ہے وہ بر بنائے ضرورت ہے، اس لئے بیوی آزاد، عاقل، بالغ عورت ہے اور آزاد ہر طرح کی قید و بند سے آزاد ہوتا ہے، مگر پھر بھی ضرورت توالد و تناسل کے تحت خلاف قیاس عورت پر شوہر کی ملکیت ثابت ہوتی ہے، اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ الضرورة تتقدر بقدرها “ یعنی خلاف قیاس ہونے والی چیز ضرور تا ہی ثابت ہوتی ہے،اس لئے شوہر کی ملک نکاح ضروری ہے اور شراء ہبہ وغیرہ کے ذریعے عورت جب اس کی ملکیت میں آجائے گی تو اسے اس پر ملک یمین حاصل ہو گی ، جو ملک قوی ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ ملک قوی کے مقابلے میں ملک ضروری باقی نہیں رہ سکتی ، اس لئے قومی ملک یمین حاصل ہوتے ہی ملک ضروری یعنی ملک نکاح ختم ہو جائے گی ۔
وَلَوْ مَلَكَهَا أَوْ شِقْصَهَا أَوْ مَلَكَتْهُ أَوْ شِقْصَهُ بَطَلَ الْعَقْدُ يَعْنِي لَوْ مَلَكَ الزَّوْجُ امْرَأَتَهُ بِأَنْ كَانَتْ أَمَةً أَوْ مَلَكَ جُزْءا مِنْهَا أَوْ كَانَتْ هِيَ الْمَالِكَةُ لِزَوْجِهَا أَوْ لِجُزْئِهِ بَطَلَ النِّكَاحُ. وَأَمَّا مِلْكُهَا إِيَّاهُ فَلِلاجْتِمَاعِ بَيْنَ الْمَالِكِيَّةِ وَالْمَمْلُوكِيَّةِ فَلَا يَنْتَظِمُ الْمَصَالِحُ وَهُوَ مَا شُرِعَ إِلَّا لِمَصَالِحِهِ، وَأَمَّا مِلْكُهُ إِيَّاهَا فَلانَّ مِلكَ النِّكَاحِ ضَرُورِيٌّ وَقَدْ اسْتَغْنَى عَنْهُ بِالْأَقْوَى لِقُبُوتِ الحل به.
تبيين الحقائق كتاب الطلاق فصل فى إضافة الطلاق إلى الزمان، ج ۲ ص ۲۰۹، ط: المطبعة الكبرى الأميرية
If he owns her or a share of her, or she owns him or a share of him, the contract is nullified. Meaning: if the husband owns his wife, as if she were a slave, or he owns a part of her, or she is the owner of her husband or a part of him, the marriage is nullified. As for her ownership of him, it is due to the combination of ownership and being owned, so the benefits (for which marriage is legislated) cannot be achieved. As for his ownership of her, it is because marriage ownership is based on necessity, and it is dispensed with by the stronger (ownership) because it is accommodated by it.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with rational proof from Hanafi fiqh. It addresses the scenario where a spouse becomes the owner of the other spouse or a portion thereof, leading to the nullification of the marriage contract. The author distinguishes two cases: (1) when the wife owns her husband or a part of him, and (2) when the husband owns his wife or a part of her. In the first case, the reason for nullification is the impossibility of simultaneously being an owner and owned in the context of marriage, which is founded on mutual rights and benefits. In the second case, the reason is that the husband's ownership over his wife through marriage (milk al-nikah) is a weaker, necessity-based ownership (for procreation), whereas ownership through purchase or gift (milk al-yamin) is a stronger, full ownership. Since necessity is limited to its extent, the stronger ownership overrides the weaker, and the marriage ends. The proof relies on the legal maxim 'al-darurah tuqaddaru biqadariha' (necessity is measured by its extent).

Key Terms
ملک نکاح (milk al-nikah): The husband's ownership over his wife by virtue of marriage, which is a legal right requiring the wife to be available for marital relations and subject to the husband's authority in certain matters.
ملک یمین (milk al-yamin): Full ownership of a person through purchase, gift, inheritance, or other means, which grants complete proprietary control over the owned person (slave).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the marriage nullify when the husband buys his own wife who is a free woman?
A) Because marriage is a contract that ends upon any change in ownership.
B) Because milk al-nikah is a necessity-based ownership and is overridden by the stronger milk al-yamin.
C) Because the wife becomes a slave, which is impermissible.
D) Because the husband cannot own both a wife and a slave simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
Marriage ownership (milk al-nikah) is a necessity-based weak ownership that is overridden by the stronger property ownership (milk al-yamin), leading to nullification of marriage when a spouse becomes the other's owner.

Marriage Substitutes for Intercourse Only Where Conceivable
Establishing a principle: marriage stands in place of intercourse only where intercourse is conceivable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that marriage substitutes for intercourse only where intercourse is conceivable, and apply it to determine whether lineage is established from a minor husband.

Core Idea
Marriage substitutes for intercourse only where intercourse is conceivable; without possibility, lineage fails.

This passage from Al-Hidayah introduces a critical limitation on the legal fiction that marriage stands in place of intercourse. While marriage generally establishes lineage and certain rulings, this substitution is conditional: it only operates where intercourse is physically conceivable. The author illustrates this with the case of a deceased minor boy whose wife is pregnant — despite the marriage, the child's lineage is not attributed to him because a minor cannot have intercourse. Understanding this principle prevents erroneous attribution of paternity.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Identify the exact wording of the principle: marriage stands in place of intercourse only in the place of conception (mawdi' al-tasawwur).
The Arabic: إن النكاح يقام مقام الولي في موضع التصور.
2
Define 'Mawdi' al-Tasawwur'
Determine what 'place of conception' means: it is where intercourse is physically conceivable. A person from whom intercourse is imaginable.
The commentary clarifies: إذا كان الوطي متصورا.
3
Apply to a Minor
Apply the principle to the case of a minor boy who dies. Since a minor cannot have intercourse, marriage does not substitute; thus, any pregnancy cannot be attributed to him.
The minor has no semen (لا ماء له).
4
Note the Exception
Consider the exception: if the wife gives birth more than two years after the husband's death, the iddah is considered to have ended earlier, and lineage is not established from the deceased in that case either.
This exception confirms the principle's limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۰۸) إِنَّ النِّكَاحَ يُقَامَ مَقَامَ الْوَلِّي فِي مَوْضِعِ التَّصَوُّرِ. ترجمہ : موضع تصور میں نکاح وطی کے قائم مقام ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نکاح وطی کا قائم مقام اس وقت ہوتا ہے جہاں ولی کا تصور ہو، جس شخص سے وطی متصور ہو تو نکاح اس کے حق میں وطی کا قائم مقام ہو گا۔ اور جہاں وطی متصور نہ ہو تو نکاح وطی کا قائم مقام نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں اگر نابالغ بچہ مرگیا جبکہ اس کی بیوی حاملہ تھی تو نسب ثابت نہ ہو گا اگر چہ یہاں نکاح قائم تھا، مذکورہ صورت میں ہم نکاح کو ولی کا قائم مقام کر کے نسب کو ثابت نہیں کر سکتے ، کیونکہ نکاح وہاں وطی کا قائم مقام ہوتا ہے جہاں وطی متصور ہو اور صغیر سے چونکہ ولی متصور نہیں ہے، لہذا نکاح کو بھی صغیر کے حق میں وطی کا قائم مقام نہیں بنا سکتے ، اس لئے نسب ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ (وَإِنْ حَمَلَتْ بَعْدَ مَوْتِ الصَّبِيِّ بِأَنْ وَلَدَتْ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ لِسِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَصَاعِدًا عَلَى مَا هُوَ الْأَصَحُ فَعِدَّتُهَا بِالْأَشْهُرٍ إِجْمَاعًا وَلَا نَسَبَ فِى الْوَجْهَيْنِ أَى فِيمَا إِذَا حَبِلَتْ قَبْلَ مَوْتِ الصَّبِيِّ أَوْ بَعْدَهُ، لأَنَّ الصَّبِيَّ لَا مَاء لَهُ فَلا يُتَصَوَّرُ الْعُلُوقُ وَفِيهِ إِشْعَارٌ بِأَنَّهُ ثَبَتَ مِنْ غَيْرِ الصَّبِيِّ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ إِلَّا إِذَا وَلَدَتْ لِأكْثَرَ مِنْ سَنَتَيْنِ فَيُحْكَمُ بِانْقِضَائِهَا قَبْلَ الْوَضْع بِسِيَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ. مجمع الأنهر : كتاب الطلاق، باب العدة، ج ۱ ص ۴۶۶، ط: دار إحياء التراث العربي الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب العدة، ج ۲ ص ۴۳۱، ط: رحمانیه
108: Indeed, marriage stands in the place of the guardian [intercourse] in the place of conception. Translation: In the place of conception, marriage stands in place of intercourse. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that marriage stands in place of intercourse only when intercourse is conceivable from that person. If intercourse is conceivable from a person, then marriage in his case is a substitute for intercourse. And where intercourse is not conceivable, marriage will not be a substitute for intercourse. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a minor boy dies and his wife becomes pregnant, lineage is not established even though a marriage existed. In this case, we cannot make marriage a substitute for intercourse to establish lineage, because marriage substitutes for intercourse only where intercourse is conceivable, and since intercourse is not conceivable from a minor, marriage cannot be considered a substitute for intercourse in his case. Therefore, lineage is not established. (And if she becomes pregnant after the death of the boy, by giving birth after his death at six months or more according to the most correct view, then her iddah is by months by consensus, and there is no lineage in both cases, i.e., whether she became pregnant before the death of the minor or after it, because the minor has no semen, so conception is not conceivable. And in it is an indication that [the pregnancy] is established from someone other than the minor in both cases, except if she gives birth after more than two years, then it is judged that her iddah had ended before delivery by six months. Majma' al-Anhur: Kitab al-Talaq, Bab al-Iddah, vol. 1 p. 466, Dar Ihya' al-Turath al-Arabi; al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Talaq, Bab al-Iddah, vol. 2 p. 431, Dar al-Rahmaniyyah.)
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage presents a key legal principle from the Hidayah: marriage (nikah) stands in the place of intercourse (wati') only where intercourse is actually conceivable. The author illustrates this with the case of a minor boy who dies leaving his wife pregnant. Even though a valid marriage existed, the child's lineage is not established from the boy because a minor is incapable of intercourse. The principle is that marriage can substitute for intercourse to establish rulings (like lineage, iddah, etc.) only when intercourse would have been possible. The Arabic text from Majma' al-Anhur confirms this: the minor has no semen, so conception cannot be attributed to him. Hence, lineage is not established regardless of whether the wife became pregnant before or after the boy's death. An exception is noted: if she gives birth more than two years after death, it indicates her iddah had ended earlier.

Key Terms
موضع التصور (mawdi' al-tasawwur): The place or situation where intercourse is conceivable or imaginable.
نكاح (nikah): Marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in Al-Hidayah, when does marriage substitute for intercourse in establishing lineage?
A) Always, because the marriage contract is sufficient.
B) Only when the husband is an adult.
C) Only when intercourse is physically conceivable.
D) Only when the wife is pregnant at the time of marriage.

Key Takeaway
Marriage substitutes for intercourse only where intercourse is conceivable; without this condition, lineage cannot be established.

Custody Rights: The Maternal Line Priority
Principle of maternal-derived custody rights with example and hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that custody rights derive from the mother's side and apply the maternal hierarchy when determining who is most entitled to custody of a child.

Core Idea
Custody rights transfer first to maternal relatives because the right originates from the mother's side.

This passage establishes a foundational rule in Hanafi custody law: the right to raise a young child (hadanah) is primarily based on the maternal line. The author of Al-Hidayah presents the principle, illustrates it with the example of maternal versus paternal grandmother, and then cites Al-Ikhtiyar to outline the full hierarchy. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly assigning custody when the mother is absent.

Guided Path
1
State the Core Principle
Read the Arabic principle: 'إِنَّ وِلَايَةَ حِضَانَةِ الْوَلَدِ تُسْتَفَادُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْأُمَّهَاتِ'. This means the guardianship of custody is derived from the mother's side. Understand that this is the basis for all custody entitlements in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the Implication
The principle implies that when the mother is not available (deceased, absent, or disqualified), the right passes to her female relatives rather than to the father's side. The author gives the example: the maternal grandmother takes precedence over the paternal grandmother, even if the maternal grandmother is more distant.
Contrast with other schools that may prioritize the father or his relatives.
3
Trace the Hierarchy from Al-Ikhtiyar
Study the hierarchy quoted: grandmothers (maternal then paternal) are closer than sisters, sisters are closer than maternal aunts, and maternal aunts are closer than paternal aunts. This ordering is based on proximity to the mother.
The hierarchy starts from the mother's mother (maternal grandmother) and goes outward.
4
Apply to a Hypothetical
Consider a child whose mother is deceased. Who is more entitled: the maternal grandmother (even if distant) or the paternal grandmother? According to the principle, the maternal grandmother is entitled. If the maternal grandmother is also deceased, then the next in line from the maternal side (e.g., maternal aunt) takes precedence over paternal relatives.
This shows that the maternal side is always preferred over the paternal side at each level.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حضانة الولد ومن أحق به
(۱۱۴) إِنَّ وِلَايَةَ حِضَانَةِ الْوَلَدِ تُسْتَفَادُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْأُمَّهَاتِ .
ترجمہ: بچے کی پرورش کرنے کی ولایت ماؤں کی طرف سے آتی ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بچے کی پرورش کرنے کا حق پہلے ان عورتوں کو حاصل ہے جو اس بچے کی ماں کی طرف سے قریبی رشتہ دار ہیں ، مثلاً نانی ، خالہ اور بہن وغیرہ۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر بچے کی ماں نہیں ہے تو پھر نانی پرورش کرنے کی زیادہ حقدار ہے بنسبت دادی کے ، اگر چہ وہ نانی بعید ہی کیوں نہ ہو، کیونکہ یہ پرورش کی جو ولایت ہے یہ ماں کی طرف سے ہے۔ ماں کی طرف سے جو اس بچے کی قریبی رشتہ دار ہیں ان کو زیادہ حق حاصل ہے بنسبت ان عورتوں کے جو باپ کی طرف سے اس بچے کے رشتہ دار ہیں، تو نانی چونکہ اس بچے کی ماں کی طرف سے رشتہ دار ہے لہذا نانی زیادہ حقدار ہوگی بنسبت دادی کے، کیونکہ دادی کے ساتھ اس بچے کا رشتہ باپ کی طرف سے ہے۔
الهداية كتاب الطلاق، باب حضانة الولد ومن أحق به، ج ۲ ص ۴۳۹، ط: رحمانیه
الأصْلُ فِي ذَلِكَ أَنَّ هَذِهِ الْوَلَايَةَ تُسْتَفَادُ مِنْ قِبَلِ الْأُمَّهَاتِ لِمَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ، فَكَانَتْ جِهَةُ الْأُمِّ مُقَدَّمَةٌ عَلَى جِهَةِ الْآبِ، وَلَانَّ الْجَدَّاتِ أَقْرَبُ مِنَ الْأَخَوَاتِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ أَقْرَبُ مِنَ الْخَالَاتِ وَالْعَمَّاتِ. الاختيار لتعليل المختار كتاب الطلاق، باب النفقة باب الحضانة، ج ۴ ص ۱۵، ط: مطبعة المجلس القاهرة
Chapter: Custody of the Child and Who Is Most Entitled to It. (114) Indeed the guardianship of custody of the child is derived from the side of the mothers. Translation: The guardianship of raising a child comes from the mothers. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the right to raise the child belongs first to those women who are close relatives of the child from the mother's side, such as maternal grandmother, maternal aunt, and sister, etc. The author of Hidayah, mentioning this principle, is explaining that if the child's mother is not present, then the maternal grandmother is more entitled to custody than the paternal grandmother, even if that maternal grandmother is distant, because this custody guardianship is from the mother's side. Those who are close relatives of the child from the mother's side have more right than those women who are relatives from the father's side. Thus, the maternal grandmother, since she is related to the child through the mother, will be more entitled than the paternal grandmother, because the paternal grandmother's relation to the child is through the father. The original principle in this is that this guardianship is derived from the side of the mothers for what we have presented, so the mother's side is given precedence over the father's side. And the grandmothers are closer than the sisters, and the sisters are closer than the maternal aunts and paternal aunts. (From Al-Ikhtiyar)
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage sets forth a foundational rule in Hanafi custody (hadanah) law: the right to custody of a young child is primarily based on the maternal line. The author states the principle and then explains it through an example: if the mother is absent, the maternal grandmother is preferred over the paternal grandmother, regardless of how distant the maternal grandmother is. This is because custody (wilayat al-hadanah) is a right that comes from the mother's side. The passage also quotes from Al-Ikhtiyar to show the hierarchy: grandmothers are closer than sisters, sisters closer than maternal aunts and paternal aunts. This establishes a clear order of entitlement rooted in the maternal connection. The commentary emphasizes that even a distant maternal relative takes precedence over a close paternal relative due to this principle.

Key Terms
حِضَانَة (ḥiḍānah): Custody and upbringing of a young child, which includes physical care and guardianship rights.
وِلَايَة (wilāyah): Authority or guardianship granted by Shari'ah to certain relatives for the care of the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy mentioned in Al-Ikhtiyar, who is closer to the child in terms of custody entitlement: a sister or a maternal aunt?
A) The sister
B) The maternal aunt
C) Both are equal
D) It depends on the child's age

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, custody rights are derived from the mother's side, making maternal relatives preferable over paternal ones at every level of the hierarchy.

Two Compensations Cannot Combine: The Hanafi Distinction Between Mahr and Nafaqah
States the maxim and its application to mahr and nafaqah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'لا يجتمع العوضان عن معوض واحد' to distinguish between mahr and nafaqah in Hanafi marriage law.

Core Idea
One thing cannot have two compensations: nafaqah is not for marriage ownership but for ihtibas.

In Hanafi fiqh, the marriage contract involves a clear exchange: the husband provides mahr in return for the right of ownership (milk al-nikah). But what about nafaqah? Is it a second compensation? The legal maxim 'two compensations cannot combine for one thing' resolves this: nafaqah must be for something else – the wife's ihtibas (confinement). This lesson unpacks the maxim and its application.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Recite the Arabic maxim 'لا يجتمع العوضان عن معوض واحد' and understand its literal meaning: two compensations cannot combine for one thing.
2
Identify the mu'awwad
In the marriage context, identify the mu'awwad (the thing being compensated) as milk al-nikah (the husband's right of ownership over his wife).
This is the exclusive subject of the marriage exchange.
3
List the compensations
Identify mahr as the compensation (iwad) for milk al-nikah. Then consider nafaqah: if it were also a compensation for the same ownership, there would be two compensations.
Mahr is explicitly the bride price.
4
Apply the maxim
Show that two compensations for one thing violate the maxim. Therefore, nafaqah cannot be compensation for milk al-nikah.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
Therefore, nafaqah is compensation for ihtibas (the wife's being at the husband's disposal), not for ownership.
This distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from the Shafi'i school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١١٩) لَا يَجْتَمِعُ الْعِوَضَانِ عَنْ مُعَوَّضٍ وَاحِدٍ.
ترجمہ: ایک معوض کے دو عوض جمع نہیں ہو سکتے ۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک ہی معوض کے بدلے دو عوض کا اجتماع نہیں ہوتا یعنی ایسا درست نہیں ہے کہ معوض ایک ہو اور عوض دو ہوں ۔
اصول ہدایہ جلد ثانی صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ احناف کے نزدیک نفقہ احتباس کا بدلہ ہے نہ کہ ملک نکاح کا عوض ، کیونکہ ملک نکاح کا عوض مہر ہے ، اب اگر نفقہ بھی ملکیت کا عوض ہو جائے تو اس صورت میں ایک معوض یعنی ملکیت کے دو عوض یعنی مہر اور نفقہ لازم آئے گا، اور ایک معوض کے دو عوض نہیں ہو سکتے ، لہذا انفقہ ملکیت کا عوض نہ ہوگا بلکہ احتباس کا بدلہ ہو گا۔
(119) Two compensations cannot combine for one thing. Translation: Two compensations cannot combine for a single thing. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that two compensations do not occur in exchange for one thing, i.e., it is not correct that the thing is one and the compensations are two. Usool-e-Hidayah Volume 2: The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is conveying that according to the Hanafis, nafaqah is the recompense for ihtibas, not the compensation for the ownership of marriage, because the compensation for ownership of marriage is mahr. Now if nafaqah were also a compensation for ownership, then in that case there would be two compensations (mahr and nafaqah) for one thing (ownership), and two compensations cannot be for one thing. Therefore, nafaqah will not be a compensation for ownership, but rather a recompense for ihtibas.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim (qa'idah) from Hanafi fiqh: one thing cannot be the subject of two different compensations. The specific application here is the distinction between mahr and nafaqah. Mahr is the compensation for the marriage contract (ownership of the wife). If nafaqah were also a compensation for that same ownership, then there would be two compensations for one thing, which is impossible. Therefore, nafaqah must be a recompense for something else, namely the wife's ihtibas (her being at the husband's disposal). This principle is used to argue against the Shafi'i view that nafaqah is compensation for ownership. The commentary explains that the Hidayah's author uses this maxim to clarify the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
عوض (ʿiwaḍ): Compensation; something given in exchange for something else.
معوض (muʿawwaḍ): The thing for which compensation is given; the subject of an exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the compensation for the ownership of marriage (milk al-nikah) according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Nafaqah
B) Mahr
C) Both mahr and nafaqah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim that two compensations cannot combine for one thing distinguishes mahr as compensation for marriage ownership from nafaqah as compensation for ihtibas.

Nafaqah is a Gift, Not a Compensation
States Hanafi principle on nafaqah as gift.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that nafaqah is a gift (silah) and explain why it does not automatically become a debt for past periods.

Core Idea
Nafaqah is a daily gift; only qadi's order or mutual agreement makes it binding for the past.

This lesson unpacks a foundational Hanafi principle about nafaqah (spousal maintenance). Unlike other schools that treat unpaid maintenance as an automatic debt, the Hanafi school views it as a periodic gift (silah). This distinction has significant practical consequences for claims of past nafaqah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The passage states: 'Nafaqah is a gift, not a compensation.' Understand that silah means a favor or recurrent payment, not an exchange (iwad).
2
Analyze the Consequence
If nafaqah is a gift, it does not automatically become a debt in the husband's liability (dhimmah) for past periods. The wife cannot claim retroactively for time that has passed.
This contrasts with the view that nafaqah is a compensation, which would accrue as a debt.
3
Recognize the Exceptions
The only ways past nafaqah becomes binding are: (1) a qadi determines it, or (2) the spouses mutually agree on a specific amount. Then it transforms into a debt.
Until one of these occurs, no obligation for the past exists.
4
Compare with Other Schools
Shafi'is treat nafaqah as iwad (compensation), so it becomes a debt from the moment of non-payment. Hanafis require formal determination.
This is a key ikhtilaf with practical differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۰) إِنَّ النَّفَقَةَ صِلَةٌ وَلَيْسَتْ بِعِوَضٍ عِنْدَنَا.
ترجمہ: ہمارے ہاں نفقہ عطیہ ہے عوض نہیں ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیوی کا نان نفقہ یہ ایک صلہ یعنی عطیہ واحسان ہے، یہ ہمارے نزدیک عوض نہیں ہے، یعنی جب تک قاضی مقرر نہ کرے یا آپس میں میاں بیوی ایک مقدار پر مصالحت نہ کریں اس وقت تک یہ مؤ کہ نہیں ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر ایک مدت گزر گئی جس میں شوہر نے بیوی کو نفقہ نہیں دیا اور بیوی نے اس گزشتہ مدت کے نفقے کا مطالبہ کیا تو اس کے لئے کچھ بھی نہیں ہوگا، البتہ اگر قاضی نے اس کے لئے نفقہ مقرر کیا تھا یا میاں بیوی نے آپس میں ایک مقدارِ نفقہ پر صلح کر لی تھی تو اس صورت میں شوہر پر گزری ہوئی مدت کا نفقہ واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ نفقہ عطیہ ہے جب تک قاضی مقرر نہ کرے یا آپس میں زوجین مصالحت نہ کریں اس وقت واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے کہ ہمارے یہاں نفقہ عوض نہیں ہے کہ ذمہ میں لازم ہو بلکہ یہ تو عطیہ ہے جو ذمہ میں لازم نہیں ہوتا ، البتہ اس کے حتمی ثبوت اور استحکام کے لئے قضائے قاضی اور مصالحت بین الزوجین
(120) Indeed, nafaqah is a gift and not a compensation according to us. Translation: According to us, nafaqah is a gift, not a compensation. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the wife's nafaqah is a gift and favor; according to us, it is not a compensation, i.e., until the qadi determines it or the husband and wife come to an agreement on an amount, it is not determined. The author of al-Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is conveying that if a period passes in which the husband did not give nafaqah to the wife and she demands nafaqah for that past period, then she will get nothing. However, if the qadi had determined nafaqah for her or the husband and wife had mutually settled on an amount of nafaqah, then in that case the nafaqah for the past period becomes obligatory on the husband, because nafaqah is a gift; until the qadi determines it or the spouses settle, it is not obligatory. Because according to us, nafaqah is not a compensation that becomes binding on the dhimmah; rather, it is a gift that does not become binding on the dhimmah. However, for its conclusive proof and stability, the determination of the qadi and the settlement between the spouses [are necessary].
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that explains the Hanafi view of nafaqah as a gift (silah) rather than a compensation (iwad). The practical implication is that nafaqah does not automatically become a debt in the husband's liability for past periods. If a wife does not receive nafaqah for some time, she cannot claim it retroactively unless a qadi had fixed the amount or the couple had mutually agreed upon it. This is because, in Hanafi fiqh, nafaqah is considered a periodic gift that arises each day; it does not accumulate as a debt from the past. The commentary clarifies that the determination by a qadi or mutual agreement converts it into a binding obligation. This view contrasts with other schools that might treat nafaqah as a fixed obligation from the moment of need.

Key Terms
صلہ (ṣilah): A gift or favor; something given voluntarily or due as a recurrent payment.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance or provision for a wife's basic needs (food, clothing, shelter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for past nafaqah to become obligatory on the husband according to the Hanafi school?
A) The wife's demand alone
B) The passage of time
C) A qadi's determination or mutual agreement
D) The husband's acknowledgement

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, nafaqah is a daily gift that becomes a debt only when fixed by a qadi or agreed upon.
